Abyssinia Makes Major Concessions, Geneva Negotiations Frequent, Laval and Hoare Suggest Meeting with Hoel, One Says Italy Will Use Troops by Late September 18

(Geneva) According to the French delegation, French Prime Minister Laval, who arrived here this morning, does indeed have a new plan to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian case. He will submit it to the League of Nations' Five-Power Committee this afternoon. Laval met with British Foreign Secretary Hoare at 11:00 AM this morning. The content of the meeting is being kept strictly confidential. (National Telegram, 10th)

(Geneva) After French Prime Minister Laval arrived here this morning, he and British Foreign Secretary Hoare jointly discussed peaceful solutions to the overall dispute. The discussion lasted for over an hour. Hoare then immediately met with Italian Chief Representative Aloisi and is scheduled to confer with Laval again this evening. (Havas Dispatch, 10th)

(Paris) Prime Minister Laval left for Geneva at 8:25 PM last night, after receiving the British and Italian ambassadors. According to the "Le Matin" newspaper, the French Prime Minister is not only concerned about the sanctions issue but also fears that the UK's resolute attitude on the sanctions issue will have a serious impact on resolving European issues such as the Danube and Eastern European pacts. A "Paris Soir" report from Rome states that Mussolini assured Laval that Italy does not oppose international co-management of Abyssinia. The prolongation of the East African war and fears of conflict between Italy and Britain are gradually causing some elements in Italy to lean towards reconciliation. The Italian government hopes that the League of Nations' Five-Power Committee will recommend international assistance to Abyssinia, placing the country under a protected status, and hopes that the details of this assistance will be determined by the signatory countries of the 1906 Tripartite Treaty. (National Telegram, 10th)

Addis Ababa. As a result of all-night discussions by the Imperial Council, a resolution has been telegraphed to Abyssinia's League of Nations representatives, stating that the Abyssinian Emperor is prepared to accept the suggestion that the Abyssinian government hire European advisors. This is the final concession. The League of Nations is free to propose any candidates, but the Abyssinian Emperor reserves the right of approval. However, he firmly rejects any suggestion to place Abyssinia under a mandate, as this would undermine Abyssinia's sovereignty and independence. The Abyssinian Emperor is also willing to cede the Ogaden Province in the southeast to Italy, and allow the construction of a highway from Italian Eritrea to Jiangda, which is in northern Abyssinia, 200 kilometers from the Italian border. He is also willing to resume the 1928 negotiations to discuss a highway from the Abyssinian capital to the Eritrean southern port of Assab. Although this news has been widely circulated, the Governor of Arusi, between Addis Ababa and Ogaden, has already been ordered to lead 25,000 troops to Ogaden for deployment. This march will take at least ten days to reach its destination. (National Telegram, 9th)

(Rome) Political circles here today are expressing doubt about the possibility of resolving the Italo-Abyssinian dispute through Geneva mediation. Someone asked the authorities, citing the Abyssinian capital's claim that the Abyssinian Emperor considered September 4th as the "final hour." The authorities shrugged and replied, "We are preparing to deal with the situation every day." This statement seems to be true, as judging from the appearances, the Italian army is currently preparing to begin its offensive at the end of September. According to a dispatch from Addis Ababa, Emperor Haile Selassie's attitude remains quite firm. It is said that the Abyssinian Emperor does not agree with the tripartite trusteeship, or the Italian protection system like Britain in Iraq, or the establishment of an Italian gendarmerie system. Furthermore, according to the Italian Embassy in Abyssinia, the actions of the Italian army in Eritrea as reported in the bulletin are merely routine and have no other significance. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

Five-Power Committee Works Very Hard, Experts Review Documents 19

(Geneva) The Special Committee of the League of Nations is now very enthusiastic in its work. If it can maintain the current pace, its work can be completed in a few days. The Italian memorandum accusing Abyssinia of not being qualified for League of Nations membership, and the Abyssinian government's promised reply, will be reviewed by a small group of experts. Representatives from Britain, France, Poland, Spain, and Turkey will join this committee. The Abyssinian Emperor has placed himself entirely at the disposal of the League of Nations. Any resolution that does not hinder the integrity of Abyssinia's territory and political independence is likely to be accepted by the Abyssinian Emperor. The UK has also officially announced its position that any suggestion for resolving the Italo-Abyssinian dispute should allow the Abyssinian government the freedom to accept or reject it. It is too early to say that Abyssinia has rejected the suggestions made in Paris or other suggestions, as no suggestions have been put forward so far. (Reuters Dispatch, 10th)

(Geneva) The Administrative Council Subcommittee of the international conference studying a peaceful resolution to the Italo-Abyssinian dispute continued to meet from 3:30 PM to 4:45 PM today. It reviewed the various files of previous negotiations. In addition, it appointed a committee of experts, chaired by Spanish representative Arivan, to be responsible for reviewing the documents submitted by both Italy and Abyssinia and making a comprehensive analysis. This committee of experts includes representatives from the countries attending the subcommittee. Once the committee of experts completes its review, the subcommittee will proceed with reconciliation work based on this review report. Regarding reconciliation methods, according to the Havas News Agency special correspondent, the League of Nations Administrative Council has broad freedom of action regarding Abyssinia, because when Abyssinia joined the League of Nations, it formally stated that it would follow all the suggestions made by the League of Nations, especially regarding the abolition of slavery, but in practice, it has not yet been effectively implemented. The chairman of the subcommittee, Spanish representative Madariaga, will be in close contact with the representatives of Italy and Abyssinia during the committee's work. Also, today's committee meeting authorized Chairman Madariaga to consult with jurists from various countries currently in Geneva in order to resolve the various legal issues arising from the Italo-Abyssinian conflict, such as the issue of reconciling the mandated territory system with the original sovereignty of League of Nations member states. The subcommittee stipulated that it would continue to adjourn tomorrow. (Havas Dispatch, 11th)

(Geneva) The Five-Power Committee mediating the Abyssinian case met this afternoon and decided to form another committee to select colonial experts from five countries as members, responsible for investigating Italy's accusations against Abyssinia and Abyssinia's defense. It is believed here that organizing a committee of colonial experts will enable Italy to obtain some satisfaction. At the same time, the Five-Power Committee is striving to find a settlement method that does not violate the League of Nations Covenant and the principle of Abyssinia's territorial integrity. However, the League of Nations is not very optimistic about the committee's efforts, as the Italian side may not be able to accept any suggestions from the committee. (National Telegram, 9th)

(London) The Times reports that the British representative on the League of Nations Administrative Council's Italo-Abyssinian Dispute Subcommittee has proposed to the subcommittee that the League of Nations establish a collective mandate system in Abyssinia. The subcommittee is currently considering two methods: one is for the League of Nations Administrative Council to directly exercise ruling power and send a senior commissioner to be stationed in Abyssinia; the other is for the signatory countries of the 1906 Treaty, namely Britain, France, and Italy, to jointly exercise mandate power. On the British side, a condition will be put forward, namely that this solution must be accepted by Abyssinia. (Havas Dispatch, 10th)

(Geneva) The Five-Power Special Committee is still committed to thoroughly investigating the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia, while rumors are arising from outside, causing great confusion. In fact, the committee has not discussed making major changes to the suggestions put forward by Paris. The Abyssinian representative has agreed to accept any resolution of the Five-Power Special Committee. (Reuters Dispatch, 10th)

(Geneva) The chairman of the Five-Power Committee, Spanish representative Daliaga, met with Italian representative Aroxi yesterday and requested the Italian government to guarantee that it would not take military action during the committee's work. The Italian side was unwilling to reply, because Italy still retains the right to freedom of action towards Abyssinia. (National News Agency Dispatch, 10th)

The League of Nations General Assembly Presidium: The Soviet Union's Failure to be Elected is Surprising 21

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly convened this morning. The fact that Soviet Russia failed to obtain a seat in the Presidium is considered surprising here. All major powers have joined the Presidium, except Russia, which was only two votes short. This matter has caused some criticism. This is the second failure for Soviet Russia. In the previous election of vice-presidents of the General Assembly, the chief representatives of six countries, namely Britain, France, Italy, Spain, Belgium, and Mexico, were all elected. Soviet Russia was ranked seventh and failed to be elected. Czech Foreign Minister Dr. Beneš was elected as Chairman of the General Assembly, and the President of the Irish Free State, Mr. de Valera, was elected as Chairman of the Political Committee. After the initial meeting procedures were completed, the General Assembly will debate the report of Secretary-General Avenol. The debate is expected to begin around Wednesday. It is expected that British Foreign Secretary Hoare will deliver his first speech at the General Assembly in his capacity as the UK's chief representative at that time. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

(Paris) The League of Nations General Assembly elected six vice-presidents yesterday, and the Soviet Union failed to be elected. This news has caused great surprise here, as it is unprecedented for a permanent member of the Administrative Council to fail to be elected. The Daily News reported that the matter was like a drama, and the number of votes obtained by the Soviet Union was less than that of Mexico, which also shows the revival of anti-Russian sentiment among Europeans and Americans. (National News Agency Dispatch, 10th)

(Geneva) The 16th League of Nations General Assembly continued to meet at 5:30 PM this afternoon to elect vice-presidents. France received 46 votes, Britain received 41 votes, Italy received 41 votes, Spain received 38 votes, Belgium received 30 votes, Mexico received 30 votes, and the Soviet Union received 29 votes. All were elected as vice-presidents.

Afterwards, the chairmen of the seven committees of the General Assembly were elected. According to the usual practice of the League of Nations General Assembly, there are seven committees. The list of elected chairmen for this session is as follows:

(1) Legal and Regulatory Committee: Dutch representative Limburg was elected as Chairman.

(2) Economic and Financial Committee: Polish representative Chvatetsky was elected as Chairman.

(3) Disarmament Committee: It was decided to temporarily suspend the organization. Budget Committee: Romanian representative Radulescu was elected as Chairman.

(5) Social Issues Committee: Countess Apponyi of Hungary was elected as Chairman.

(6) Political Issues Committee: Mr. de Valera, representative of the Irish Free State, was elected as Chairman.

(7) Agenda Committee: Swiss representative Motta, Chairman. In addition, the by-election to fill the vacancy of the late Japanese judge Adachi of the Hague International Permanent Court will be decided by the Chairman and Vice-Chairmen of the General Assembly tomorrow. The re-election of the three non-permanent members of the Administrative Council whose terms have expired, Poland, Czechoslovakia, and Mexico, is scheduled to be held on September 16. The General Assembly is now scheduled to hold a plenary session on Wednesday morning, at which British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval will deliver speeches. As for tomorrow's meeting, it will be dedicated to arranging the work of the various committees. (Havas Dispatch, 9th)

Polish Elections, Number of Voters Greatly Reduced, Actually Accounting for 28.3 Percent 27

Warsaw According to the official provisional results of yesterday's House of Representatives election, out of 16,583,000 registered voters, 7,576,687 people participated in the voting, that is, the number of voters only accounted for 46.5 percent of the total number of voters. In the 1930 election, the number of voters accounted for 74.8 percent. It can be seen that the number of voters has decreased by 28.3 percent compared with the previous election. In Warsaw, the number of voters was only 30 percent, and in the cities of Łódź and Kraków, it was 37 percent, but in the provinces of Silesia and Volhynia, the voter turnout rate was higher. Also, during yesterday's voting, most voters, although they did not give up their right to vote, cast many invalid votes. It is estimated that out of the total of more than 7 million votes cast nationwide, up to one million were invalid votes. This layer was not mentioned in the official report. The government explained the reason for the low voter turnout, saying that it was due to bad weather and the opposition party's movement to boycott voting. However, the general public believes that it is a kind of expression of the people's opposition to the new election law, which can be said to be a failure on the part of the government. Among the 208 newly elected members of the House of Representatives, Poles account for 184 seats, Ukrainians account for 19 seats, Jews account for 4 seats, Russians account for 1 seat, and the German ethnic group was not elected. In addition, there are two women in the new House of Representatives. (Havas Dispatch, 9th)

Huilang Dies; Dying Words Unceasing; Roosevelt Deeply Saddened 28

Baton Rouge: Senator Huey Long, after being shot yesterday, died at Lakeside Hospital at 4:10 this morning. His death had been predicted by doctors hours earlier, as his large intestine was pierced and the bullet had deeply penetrated his intestines, causing internal bleeding that could not be stopped, even after four blood transfusions. Long remained conscious until his death, but was in severe pain and unable to speak. The Governor of Louisiana and his closest friends and family were at his side when he died. State officials immediately took measures to prevent riots. (Ninth National Telegram)

Hyde Park, USA: Upon hearing the news of Senator Huey Long's assassination today, President Roosevelt said, "I am deeply saddened by this action, as the use of violence is contrary to the spirit of America and does not benefit national affairs. Especially now, we should approach difficult problems with a calm and peaceful attitude." It is noted that Huey Long had recently been one of Roosevelt's fiercest critics. (Ninth National Telegram)

Baton Rouge: Upon hearing the report of Senator Long being shot in the Louisiana State Capitol by Dr. Weiss in Hyde Park, New York, President Roosevelt said today that he deeply regretted this assassination. Violence is not in the American spirit and has no place in the consideration of public affairs. Especially today, when handling difficult issues must be done with a calm and rational attitude, violence cannot be tolerated. A hospital bulletin stated that Long's wounds were expected to heal, but according to reliable sources, Long's condition has worsened. A blood transfusion at noon strengthened his pulse, but a second transfusion is needed. Although armed rebellion is unlikely in Louisiana, the atmosphere throughout the state is tense. State police are being deployed to Baton Rouge to protect the Capitol and the hospital where Long is being treated, and the National Guard is prepared to support the police if necessary. The police chief has ordered police to shoot anyone photographing inside or outside the Capitol or hospital. The assassin, Dr. Weiss, was shot dead on the spot by Long's guards. His family has not yet been able to explain the reason for the assassination. Judge Pavie, Weiss's uncle, said that the matter was unrelated to Long's proposal to remove him from his judicial position. The Common Good Association, an anti-Long organization, has not issued a statement, but Long's party is in a state of anxiety. It is reported that Long's guards had received warnings to prevent accidents. If Long dies from his injuries, Louisiana's dictatorial system and wealth redistribution movement will collapse, as Long single-handedly created the political situation in Louisiana. Some predict that if Long dies, Louisiana will have a period of peace, and the state's debt of $100 million can be addressed. (Ninth Reuters Telegram)

Baton Rouge: Louisiana's dictator, Huey Long, died this morning from his injuries. His condition worsened after midnight. Although he received four blood transfusions, his pulse increased to 118, and he was delirious, constantly mumbling about his planned book, "My First Year in the White House." Doctors used oxygen therapy and planned a fifth blood transfusion, but they felt Long had fallen into a coma and there was nothing more they could do. At 4:30 AM, Dr. Anderson, the hospital director, told reporters that Long had a faint breath and the doctors had done their best, but there was no hope. Long passed away at 6:00 AM. Shortly after, his wife and three children left the hospital, their faces covered in tears. Long's last words were, "I don't know what will become of my poor college students," referring to Louisiana State University, which Long strongly supported. Governor Allen of Louisiana stated that the greatest economic builder Louisiana has produced, the likes of which have not been seen in the past 25 years, has passed away. He was a champion of human rights in America, and his name will never be forgotten in Louisiana and throughout the United States. With Long's death, President Roosevelt will have one less formidable opponent in next year's election. The assassin, Dr. Weiss, was buried this afternoon in the local cemetery, with hundreds of people attending, mostly from the Baton Rouge medical community and members of the Common Good Association, an anti-Long group. The House of Representatives met last night and did not mention Long's assassination, but passed a bill to prevent Judge Pavie, the assassin Weiss's uncle and Long's political opponent, from being re-elected. Long was born on August 30, 1893, into a poor family. His father was a pig farmer. Long graduated from a rural school, but attended university and law school for one year each. He later worked as a book and lard salesman. He became a lawyer in 1915 and served as a railroad commissioner, public service commissioner, governor, and was elected to the Washington Senate in 1930. Long became the sole political figure in the state, and under his power, Louisiana became a dictatorial state within the United States. Except for churches and the publishing industry, no public undertaking was not under his control. He held absolute power and allowed no interference from opposing parties. (Tenth Reuters Telegram)

New Orleans, USA: From all indications here today, if Senator Huey Long does not recover, the political dictatorship in Louisiana will be completely destroyed because Long's associates control state affairs. These people will start infighting as soon as Long dies. Today, Long's wife and two children visited him at the hospital. When they left, they seemed calm and said that Long had said when he entered the hospital, "I may not return home, but I am determined to fight to the death." (Ninth National Telegram)

Baton Rouge, USA: Senator Huey Long, who was seriously injured in yesterday's assassination, is now completely hopeless. His friends emerged from the sickroom and said that Senator Long would probably not survive the night. Doctors have used oxygen resuscitation and have performed the third and fourth blood transfusions. Later, a dozen doctors gathered to discuss the final rescue plan. Outside the sickroom, Long's family and the Governor of Louisiana were holding their breath, and frequently approached the bedside, their weeping audible. Long's mind is still clear, but he cannot speak, and he can still recognize his wife. He shows a weak smile each time he sees her. The whole state is very silent today, and the state government organization is also showing signs of shaking. Everyone is contemplating what will happen after Long's death. Three regiments of state troops have been mobilized in New Orleans today, and the state House of Representatives has extended its session until tomorrow morning. After receiving the bill, the state Senate will likely pass it quickly. The murderer, Weiss, was killed on the spot by Long's guards. A simple funeral was held today, attended by thousands of people. Prominent anti-Long leaders, such as Congressman Sanders and former Governor Parker, stood bareheaded in the heavy rain to express their condolences. (Ninth National Telegram)

(Washington) National political commentators, observers, and professional politicians today have various speculations about Senator Huey Long's injuries. It is generally believed that whether or not there is hope, it will ultimately affect the national political situation. If he does not recover, the political power in Louisiana will collapse, and the possibility of a third party being formed in the American South to compete with Roosevelt in next year's election will disappear. However, if he recovers, he may gain popular support as a martyr and may be able to regain the prestige he has recently lost. (Ninth National Telegram)

(Washington) The Republican National Committee issued a statement today, stating that in President Roosevelt's correspondence with Howard, chairman of the Howard newspaper group, the President said that business has had a chance to breathe, which is actually useless because what the industrial, commercial, and financial sectors need is a complete cessation of the New Deal, not a chance to breathe. The President and Howard's mutual promotion seems to be an attempt to give Howard an excuse to maintain his narrow attitude in his newspapers to support the President and advocate Roosevelt's re-election. The President certainly does not want such a famous journalist to raise embarrassing questions, so Howard has never mentioned issues such as inflation, budget balance, and the President's desire to force the Constitution to align with socialist policies. (Ninth National Telegram)

Greek Restoration Issue; Athens Experiences Another Incident; Republican Military Officer Leader Injured 29

Athens: Last night at midnight, while the cabinet was meeting to discuss holding a referendum to resolve the restoration issue, a fierce conflict erupted outside the building between General Panayotakos, leading Republican military officers, and guards belonging to the monarchist faction. For a time, the entire city of Athens was thrown into chaos, fearing that Greece would once again experience a large-scale civil war. Panayotakos and his brother were both injured and have been sent to the hospital for treatment. With Panayotakos injured, the Republican elements in the army are without a leader, so the overall situation is very bleak. Panayotakos had summoned the national garrisons in an attempt to prevent Army Chief Kondylis from pressuring Prime Minister Tsaldaris to declare support for the restoration. Kondylis, known for his strong tactics, immediately ordered Panayotakos's arrest, but the Republican warlords, with the support of the Prime Minister, refused to submit, and the war broke out. Dozens of people were arrested in the operation. The cabinet meeting was abruptly ended. When the Prime Minister stepped out of the cabinet meeting room, he reportedly told a delegation of royalists waiting at the door that he strongly supported the restoration. (Tenth Reuters Telegram)

Athens: Greek Prime Minister Tsaldaris, who returned from vacation in southern Germany yesterday, declared that the public vote to resolve the restoration issue will be held as planned. Today, rumors are rampant, indicating that the cabinet is divided on the issue of restoring the monarchy. It is claimed that Army Chief Kondylis and the Minister of Finance and Foreign Affairs threatened to resign at today's cabinet meeting because they did not agree with Tsaldaris's view that the government must remain neutral before the vote. Kondylis said that the restoration is a done deal because two-thirds of the people are inclined toward the monarchy. (Ninth National Society Telegram)

Athens: Greek Prime Minister Tsaldaris issued a notice today ordering the holding of a referendum to decide the restoration issue. If public opinion favors restoration, the deposed King George will return to Greece. Greece declared itself a republic on April 13, 1924. (Tenth Reuters Telegram)

US Mine Owners Dissatisfied with Silver Purchase Plan 30

(Washington) Mining representatives told the Associated Press today that mine owners are very dissatisfied with the government's silver purchase plan. When Congress passed the silver enhancement bill, it originally hoped to raise the price of silver to $1.29 per ounce, but the current policy of the Ministry of Finance is not only far from this standard, but also tends to depress the market price by dumping its accumulated silver. However, although mine owners are dissatisfied with the policy of the Ministry of Finance, they also recognize that general business has indeed improved considerably. (Ninth National Telegram)

Japan-Egypt Trade Negotiations; Japan's Policy Determined 31

(Tokyo) The Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Finance, Commerce and Industry, Communications, and Agriculture and Forestry will hold a joint meeting this afternoon to decide on instructions for the Japanese-Egyptian trade talks. The representative will take these instructions to Egypt to attend the meeting and begin negotiations. It is reported that the content of the instructions is generally as follows:

(1) The Japanese government advocates continuing to adopt the Japanese-Egyptian Treaty of Commerce established in 1930.

(2) The Egyptian government intends to adopt measures such as compensatory exchange tax and import allocation system to prevent the entry of Japanese cotton cloth. However, the Egyptian government should first note that Japan is a country that purchases a large amount of Egyptian cotton, and the implementation of the allocation system will result in sacrifices for the consumer class, and it is hoped that British and Egyptian exporters will benefit.

(3) Last year, Japan exported 46.79 million yuan of cotton cloth, 8.07 million yuan of rayon, 3.6 million yuan of silk fabrics, and 620,000 yuan of ceramics and porcelain to Egypt. The exports are centered on cotton cloth. Egypt only exports cotton to Japan. Therefore, the adoption of an allocation quota system is very unfavorable to Japan, so Japan opposes the adoption of this system. (Tenth Japan United Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Japan-Egypt trade conference will soon be held in Cairo. The relevant ministries decided on countermeasures at a meeting of relevant ministry officials at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 10th. As a result, the outline of the instructions carried by Representative Kasama was determined. However, Egypt is different from India. The main customer of Egyptian cotton is Britain, and Japan only ranks third. Therefore, if a commodity exchange system is adopted between Egyptian cotton and Japanese cotton products, it will be unfavorable. Therefore, it will proceed based on most-favored-nation treatment. Representative Kasama, after negotiating the detailed agreement, is scheduled to depart from Tokyo on September 18, take the Yasukuni Maru, which sets sail from Kobe on the 20th, to Singapore, and then take a regular flight to Cairo. (Tenth Electric Communication Telegram)

Japan's Three Elders Decide; Mochizuki to Succeed as Minister of Communications 32

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Okada convened a meeting of the three elders at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 10th and nominated Keisuke Mochizuki as the full-time Minister of Communications. Then, he attended a cabinet meeting to request understanding. At 3:00 PM, he met with Mochizuki, obtained his consent, and then met with the Emperor to request approval. The inauguration ceremony will be held sometime tomorrow. (Tenth Japan United Telegram)

South Manchuria Deputy President; Eight Days Decision to Resign 33

(Dalian) The Deputy President of the South Manchuria Railway Company is scheduled to meet with Ambassador to Manchuria General Minami in Dalian Zhao Changchun on the evening of the 10th to formally express his intention to resign. (Eighth Japan United Telegram)

Siamese Military Officers Plot Mutiny; One Sentenced to Death; Eight to Life Imprisonment, Three to Twenty Years 34

Bangkok: Fifteen Siamese junior military officers accused of plotting to rebel were sentenced today by a special court. One person was sentenced to death, eight to life imprisonment, three to ten years' imprisonment, and one to sixteen years' imprisonment, totaling thirteen people. Eleven of them confessed to their crimes. They conspired to assassinate Mr. Phra Pradit, known as the "Siamese Miracle," and other important figures, including the Chairman of the Regency Council. Mr. Phra is currently en route to Europe. (Eighth Reuters Telegram)

Soviet Russia Decides to Dredge the Moscow-Volga Canal 35

(Moscow) The resolution of the Soviet People's Committee and the Central Committee of the All-Union Communist Party on the dredging of the Moscow-Volga Canal has been announced. The resolution pointed out that the project began in July 1932 and is currently progressing very smoothly, so the original plan can be expanded. The resolution approved the canal plan, stipulating that the Volga River will supply Moscow with a large amount of water, supply the Moscow River with river water, and raise its water level. Moscow will have 150 million horsepower of hydroelectric power, and Moscow and the Volga will have deep-water navigation. The project is budgeted at 1.4 billion rubles, including 980 million rubles for the construction of hydropower technology. The main projects of the canal are to excavate 135 million cubic meters of soil, install 2.9 million cubic meters of cement, and 28,000 tons of metal structures. The resolution stipulates that this project must be completed before the 1937 navigation season, at which time navigation will begin. (Ninth TASS Telegram)

(Moscow) The Soviet People's Committee and the Central Committee of the All-Union Communist Party resolved to expand the original plan for the Moscow-Volga Canal. Pravda commented, "The Soviet government has begun dredging the canal. This canal is the largest river canal in the world. It has strong economic and technical equipment. Today, we can build everything on an unprecedented scale and in the shortest time to improve and beautify people's daily lives and make the lives of socialist builders extremely pleasant." (Tenth TASS Telegram)

German Balloon Confiscated by Czechoslovakia 36

(Berlin) According to the German official news agency, four German private balloons flew over a military camp in Miro, Czechoslovakia, and were surrounded by Czech military aircraft, forced to land, and confiscated. (Ninth National Telegram)

International Commerce

—Reuters Special Telegram, September 10—

Gold and Silver

English Gold: London gold price fell 6.5 pence today to 140 shillings and 7.5 pence.

English Silver: The London silver market was unchanged today. Spot and futures prices remained at 29.1875 pence. American purchases and Chinese buying and selling activities kept the market stable.

Exchange Rates

British-American: In the London foreign exchange market this morning, European buyers purchased British pounds, causing the exchange rate against the US dollar to skyrocket. The opening exchange rate was $4.93625, higher than the US-UK closing rate yesterday by 125. At noon, it continued to rise by 5625. It fell by 125 at 1:00 PM, but rose again at 2:00 PM to $4.943125.

British-French: The opening price fell by 2 pounds sterling to 74 francs 88. It rose by 8 pounds sterling at noon, and then continued to rise by 2 pounds sterling to 74 francs 98.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened at a price up 9 pounds sterling due to strong buying interest from foreign merchants and peers. However, short selling resumed after the opening, causing prices to fall by 5 pounds sterling around 11:00 AM. Buying interest resumed at the time of the cable broadcast, and the market price rebounded by 3 pounds sterling.

English Cotton: There was very little trading in the Liverpool cotton market. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was 5.73, down 1 pound sterling. English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market opened steadily. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price fell by 25 to 5 shillings 10.875 pence. The market was stagnant.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat and grains market opened this morning at a price up 125. It continued to rise by 25 at 11:00 AM. There was profit-taking later, causing wheat and grain prices to fall by 125 to half a cent.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market continued to be quiet. The opening price for January-February futures was 5.6875 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price. It was unchanged at noon. New York: The New York rubber market opened surprisingly steadily, but trading was very light, as the market was waiting for the development of the European situation. At the time of the cable broadcast, the market price was 2 pounds sterling higher than the opening price. Trading remained inactive.

Securities

New York: The New York stock market opened sluggishly this morning. All stocks, except for oil stocks and movie stocks, were lower than yesterday's closing prices. Some fell by as much as 75. The decline stopped at 11:00 AM, and prices mostly rose slightly afterward. The average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks opened at 132.36, down 11 pounds sterling. Ministry of Railways Revises; Higher-Grade Freight Rates; Effective from the Eleventh of Next Month 37

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Railways yesterday issued a notice to its various railway bureaus, instructing them to follow the recently revised freight grade and its freight rates. Among them, two items, Zongye and goat wool (uncompressed), were added to the name list of special light and bulky goods, and the freight rates for special light and bulky goods will be charged. Raw ramie (bundled), ramie, flax, and other four items, which were previously classified as fourth-class, have now been reduced by one grade and will be charged as fifth-class. For paintings (only applicable to less-than-carload rates), the rate will be first-class for valuable items and third-class for ordinary items. Valuable items are limited to those with artistic value, while ordinary items are not. If they are printed materials, they will still be subject to temporary appraisal as usual. All of the above items will be implemented from October 11 of this year. (Tenth Central News Agency Telegram)

Beijing-Belgian Embassy Yesterday Held; Mass Service for Belgian Queen; Representatives of the National Government and Various Officials Attended 38

(Nanjing) The Beijing-Belgian Embassy held a mass service at the Catholic Church at 11:00 AM on the 10th to commemorate the late Belgian Queen. The hall was filled with wreaths presented by Chairman Lin and President Wang. In addition to Belgian Ambassador Ji Youmu personally greeting the attendees, the following also attended: National Government representatives Ye Chucang, President Wang, Kong Xiangxi, He Yingqin, Chen Gongbo, Huang Musong, Wei Huai, Xu Mo, Chen Xunyong, Peng Xuepei, Ma Chaojun, and various directors and representatives from various agencies under the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as diplomatic and consular officials from various countries stationed in Beijing, and Belgian expatriates in Beijing, totaling over a hundred people. After everyone entered the hall, a priest led the mass service. The ceremony was extremely solemn. The service ended at 12:00 PM, and the Belgian Ambassador stood at the door to shake hands with the attendees and express his gratitude. (Tenth Central News Agency Telegram)

Relief Society Handles Disaster Relief Situation 43

(Nanjing) According to Zhou Yi-kui, the head of the relief affairs department of the Relief Society, of the one million yuan in relief funds, 50,000 yuan was initially allocated to Shandong Province for urgent relief, and 40,000 yuan was for epidemic prevention expenses in various provinces. The remaining 910,000 yuan has been allocated 890,000 yuan according to the decision of the Executive Yuan, and there is now a remaining of 20,000 yuan. 10,000 yuan will be used for disaster relief in Ningxia Province and will be remitted soon, and another 10,000 yuan will be allocated to Xinjiang for epidemic prevention expenses, which will be handed over to the Ministry of Health for distribution. From August 1st to the present, the society has received over 120,000 yuan in donations from all parties, designated for flood relief and already deposited into the society's account at the Central Bank. Peiping-Shenyang Train Adds Five Armed Cars 64

The armed cars are converted from two third-class passenger cars, numbers 192 and 198. Inspection Report on River Disaster Conditions - Special Correspondent Geng Ya Reports From Dongzhuang to Xuzhou

Returning to Kaifeng from Dongzhuang, along the embankment, first passing through Zhukou, which is the second most dangerous engineering structure in Shandong. The main current of the Yellow River, coming from the northwest, once it impacts the great embankment, abruptly turns eastward. The embankment is in imminent danger. Fortunately, everyone is alarmed by the great disaster at Dongzhuang, supervising and protecting it. The embankment workers also know their responsibilities are crucial and are particularly courageous, finally turning danger into safety and singing the triumphant song of "Man will conquer nature." Entering the territory of Hebei, passing through Liuzhuang, the tense atmosphere of dike defense is no different from what was seen when coming. Traveling westward, the river surface gradually widens, the main current flows in the middle, and the waves are turbulent. The flow on both sides is gentler, and the waves are small like scales. Near the shore, there are no ripples at all. The color of the water is also different. The red embankment and green willows are completely reflected. However, the flow of the Yellow River is unpredictable. The azure blue reflects the water surface, as smooth as a mirror, but the bottom of the embankment is often hollowed out by undercurrents, which are more difficult to prevent than rat holes or badger burrows. As the saying goes, "The water of the Yellow River comes from the sky," which refers to this kind of phenomenon that is impossible to guard against. Later, entering Henan Province, the willows on the bank are lush, the river is wide and the flow is far, and the water is no longer seen. The dikes are high and thick, and dangerous places are replaced with stone works. After years of repair and protection, the foundation is increasingly consolidated. This autumn's protection project is actually easier to start than in Shandong and Hebei. However, the riverbed is much higher than the ground, which is ultimately not a fortunate thing for the future. The Huiji River, which diagonally runs through Kaifeng, Chenliu, Qixian, Suixian, and other places, does not have enough water source. In the twenty-first year of the Republic, the government specially purchased eight siphon pipes, intending to install them separately at Liuyuankou and Heigangkou, to draw water from the Yellow River to supplement its source. This is to use the principle of high river and low ground to achieve the effect of water conservancy. At Liuyuankou (thirty to forty li north of Kaifeng city), two siphon pipes were installed last winter, and the water flowed out quite smoothly. If all six remaining pipes are installed, the water drawn out, after being clarified in the water pond, flows into the Huiji River, which can irrigate 200,000 mu of land. The Yellow River flow can be reduced. If the downstream areas are expanded, the benefits will be immeasurable.

Returning to Kaifeng, taking the Longhai night train eastward, suddenly there was a commotion in the first-class carriage at Xinglong Station. Upon inquiry, it was learned that a newly boarded male passenger, seeing that other compartments were crowded, shared a compartment with a female passenger but slept in separate berths. The ticket inspector said that because the genders were strangers, it was inconvenient to share a compartment on the train, even though there were no explicit regulations, but custom had become a rule, and all railway lines followed it carefully, firmly ordering the male passenger to move to another compartment. The male passenger then said that they had just exchanged pleasantries and learned that the lady was a student at a university in Nanjing, and he was an employee of a cultural organization in Shanghai. Although they were not old acquaintances, they were both intellectuals. If he was forced to move to another compartment, it would clearly be guarding against some kind of relationship, no less than despising their personalities, and trampling on the personality of Chinese people by Chinese people. He argued on principle and refused to comply. Later, after others persuaded him, the matter was settled. The male passenger's personality was strong, but the railway authorities were also meddlesome. Twenty li northwest of the station, there is a legend of the tomb of Cangjie and the platform for creating characters, with a tall monument standing, and lush trees. Eight li east of Luo Wang Station, there is Liu Hou's tomb, with towering ancient trees, vaguely visible.

Lanfeng Station is two li away from the county seat. The terrain of the urban area is lower than the Yellow River, and the old course of the Yellow River is close to the city walls. Every time there is a flood season, there is great concern about accidents. There is a motor road that leads west to Kaifeng and northeast to Kaocheng. From Eryiji to the Yellow River Estuary, it is also accessible by car. The main product is peanuts, with about 10,000 tons shipped to Shanghai and Qingdao annually. The stations in the east and west are all known for producing peanuts. Neihuang Station is named after Neihuangji, which belongs to Qixian. The market town was formerly Waihuang County. Xiang Yu attacked it unsuccessfully and angrily wanted to bury its people alive. A thirteen-year-old retainer, Er, persuaded Xiang to spare them. The people of the town cherished his virtue and built a shrine to him, which still exists today. Minquan County was formerly Libaji, belonging to Suixian. A new county was established in the seventeenth year of the Republic. The city is seven li away from the station and is now gradually becoming prosperous. Liuhe belongs to Ningluxian, with abundant products, annually shipping wheat, soybeans, and miscellaneous grains to various counties in western Henan, and peanuts and melon seeds to Shanghai and other places, each about 1,000 tons. There are also saltpeter, alkali, and wooden boards, which are also sold to the east and west of the railway, in varying amounts each year, from hundreds of tons. The station is 200 li northeast of the Dongzhuang opening. It is heard that the Dike Closure Committee will borrow the old track materials from the Jiaoji Railway and lay them from here to Dongzhuang to transport stone materials for closing the opening. First, dams are built on both sides to occupy the area, and then stones are thrown in the middle to join them. This is a shortcut, and the method is especially good. It is hoped that it will be implemented quickly and not delayed any further.

Shangqiu, the ancient capital of Emperor Ku, was the place where Shang Tang moved to reside in Nanhao, located in the southeast of the county. It was later the State of Song and is now the leading county in eastern Henan, where the Second District Administrative Inspectorate is located. There are many agencies in the city, especially schools. Secondary education includes provincial high schools, county normal schools, and jointly established agricultural and forestry schools, and private Cuiying schools. Primary education includes the normal school affiliated high school, the county girls' high school, the first high school, and ten elementary schools. There are Guidet Daily and Yudong Guide newspapers. Financial institutions include the Henan Agricultural and Industrial Bank, and five or six Datong Silver Houses. Historical sites include the Mausoleum of Emperor Ku, 45 li south of the city, the Mausoleum of Suirenshi, northwest of Botai, and the Xili Shrine, about three li southeast of the city, where Confucius came to Song and practiced rituals with his disciples under a large tree. Later generations built a shrine to worship him, and Wenyatai, a stone monument with a portrait of the Supreme Sage painted by Wu Daozi, Zhang Xun's Tomb, is located on the plateau north of the city, the Kaiyuan Temple, built in the Tang Dynasty, with Yan Zhenqing writing the inscription and calligraphy, engraved on a stone pillar, with Ming people building a pavilion to cover it, Gaoqiu, three li southwest of the city, is the tomb of Botai, the Xiaolie General Temple, in Yingguozhen, southeast of the county, dedicated to Hua Mulan, who took her father's place in the army, with the eighth day of the fourth month as her false birthday, incense is prosperous, and there is a large output of miscellaneous grains, cattle and sheep skins, and industrial products, such as Wanshou silk and various kinds of printed cloth bedsheets, are also quite popular in various counties in western Henan and Hao County in Anhui. Hao County is more than a hundred li away from here and can be reached by car. Mamuji, forty li southeast of the city, is located near the railway and has prosperous commerce, known as "Little Guide, that is, Shangqiu". Dongxing passed Yangji Station again and entered Dangshan County, Jiangsu.

Dangshan County City, 3 li southwest of the station, 50 li south of the city, has Dangshan Mountain, from which the county gets its name. Now it belongs to Yongcheng County, Henan. There are the Tomb of Chen Sheng and the Tomb of Prince Xiao of Liang. The area is covered with mulberry fields, with trees everywhere, which is very different from the sorghum and cotton fields all over Henan Province. Because the breach at Dongzhuang has not been blocked, the Yellow River's water is invading southern Jiangsu, causing disasters in Pei and Feng counties, and Dangshan is gradually being affected. The future is worrying. Products include wheat, soybeans, Dangshan pears, daylilies, etc., with a total of more than 20,000 tons shipped to Tianjin, Shanghai, and other ports annually. Although it is threatened by the Yellow River this autumn, the area has not had rain for a long time, and the crops are withered and yellow, showing drought. The train passed Haozhai and was about to reach Tongshan. It rained at noon, and the weather suddenly cooled.

Disembarking at Xuzhou, I happened to see a company of soldiers, about a company's worth, carrying shovels and hoes, walking quickly across the overpass from the station. Behind them were twenty or thirty laborers, carrying hemp bags in pairs, their footsteps resounding on the ground, their expressions particularly tense. Their purpose, I was sure I knew it without having to ask. I unloaded my luggage at the Huayuan Hotel and then went to the Qingliange Zaotang for a bath. The noises from each seat were deafening, and most of them were talking about the disaster prevention situation. Some criticized Shandong Province for its negligence in breaching the dike and the delay in closing the opening. Others regretted that the construction of dikes in northern Jiangsu had little effect and advocated that a way out for the Yellow River water should be sought as soon as possible. The people were fearful, sighing and lamenting. The extent of the flood disaster in Xuzhou could be imagined. A pamphlet on business improvement was posted on the wall of the bathhouse, stating that in view of the current social and economic difficulties and the promotion of a new lifestyle, in order to develop business and save money for customers, prices had been reduced and no tips were accepted. The arrangement was clean and tidy, and the prices were indeed not expensive. I tried to give a tip, but they politely declined. No wonder the various businesses in Xuzhou were depressed, but this bathhouse was thriving. Those who tried to imitate it failed because they were not thorough enough. As the saying goes, "Those who earn five cents of profit starve to death, while those who earn three cents of profit are well-fed." This is indeed the business strategy of changing tricks to win in today's light-duty market.

Page 8

Impressions of a Southern Tour

— Special Correspondent Qian Hua

Since the completion of the People's Militia organization in Guizhou Province and the rigorous training of village chiefs by cadres, the grassroots foundation of the People's Militia has become increasingly stable. The most obvious result is the complete eradication of bandits in the province. Guizhou Province has a vast territory and sparse population, making it extremely easy for bandits to hide. Moreover, they would be suppressed in one place and flee to another, making it impossible to wipe them out with military force alone. Therefore, before the twentieth year of the Republic of China, Guizhou Province had a large number of bandits, entrenched in various places, causing harm to travelers and merchants. Almost as soon as the People's Militia organization succeeded, villages had self-defense forces, and they surrounded and suppressed the bandits in all directions, eliminating all the bandits. The areas where the People's Militia showed the greatest strength in suppressing bandits were Liu, Qing, Xun, Wu, and Yu, followed by Pinggui and Yong. The left and right rivers also had considerable achievements. According to local authorities, there are no traces of bandits left in the province. In remote mountainous areas, there may still be a few bandits, but at most no more than ten people in each place. They are trying to track them down and encircle them, and they expect to wipe them all out within the year. The reporter traveled by car along the highway for six days, driving more than six thousand miles, and the journey was extremely peaceful, with no traces of bandits. Mr. Pan Xinchao of the Fourth Army Group Headquarters, who accompanied me, did not carry any weapons. The car drove through desolate areas where there were no people for several hours and no armed guards. This was an opportune time for ambush, but they were able to travel unhindered. When approaching Longzhou, it was already after 7:00 PM. The car was driving through the mountains, and the evening clouds were closing in. The car had to use headlights to see the road and move forward slowly. There was no one to call for help in front or behind. Anyone with a gun on the road could have robbed the entire car and escaped leisurely, but it was also peaceful. This proves that the claim that there are no bandits in Guizhou Province is true. Facts speak louder than words. The reporter originally planned to drive back to Nanning from Longzhou on a moonlit night. Mr. Pan, who was traveling with me, said that the moonlight illuminates the mountain scenery, and there is poetry everywhere. It would be best to bring wine along, but unfortunately the sky was cloudy that night, so it did not happen. The local news in the newspapers in Shanghai is full of reports of robbery and looting, whereas the peace on the roads in Guizhou and the absence of bandits are examples to be followed. Along the way, Mr. Pan pointed out to me and said, "This is where bandits used to come and go, this is the lair of bandits." Now travelers are passing along the road, farmers and villagers are carrying things back and forth, bustling and peaceful. It is completely different from the past. As for the remnants of the Communist Party members Zhang Yuanqun, Li, and Rui in Guizhou Province, they have long been wiped out with the cooperation of the People's Militia. Last year, when Xiao Ke, Zhu De, and other troops of the western expedition passed through the area, the People's Militia of Guiliu and Pingse counties assisted the army in defense and suppression, encircling and attacking them head-on, killing 5,000 bandits. The army captured 7,000, and the People's Militia captured about 5,000, seizing hundreds of light and heavy machine guns and tens of thousands of rifles. The People's Militia and army suffered about 2,000 casualties, while the bandits suffered more than 20,000 casualties. Secondly, the People's Militia is engaged in road construction. The counties assign this work of provincial, county, and township roads to the soldiers of the People's Militia reserve teams. In addition to paying for bridge and culvert construction, the rest is compulsory labor. It is estimated that the province has completed more than 20,000 li of county roads, and about 10,000 li are open to traffic. Those not yet open to traffic must wait for the completion of bridges and culverts and the removal of stone obstacles before they can be opened to traffic. Those counties where the provincial capital of Nanning can be reached directly from the gates of the county government via the highway have reached 70%. The 30% of counties that cannot be reached are actively under construction. The entire provincial road network can be completed within next year. Completing tens of thousands of miles of roads in about two years with the least amount of money is entirely due to the People's Militia. It is a pity that the time was too rushed, and the road surface engineering was too hasty. Moreover, the slope angles and other aspects do not conform to the principles of engineering, so every time there is a flash flood, the road surface and bridges are often washed away, causing traffic congestion and requiring time for repairs, which is a major shortcoming. The next is afforestation. The counties are actively engaged in afforestation at the order of the Guizhou Provincial Government. They are now being carried out step by step by the village governments supervising the reserve teams. Although there are no significant results, they are already roughly scaled. It is estimated that the counties reported afforestation of more than 13 million trees in 1934, although only 25 counties, and the number of trees in various farms and forests has reached more than 370,000. The next is conscription. The majority of the people in Guizhou Province have a considerable understanding of the policy of placing soldiers in the militia after several years of training in the People's Militia. Therefore, the results of the first conscription order were quite remarkable. The enthusiasm of volunteers to enlist, especially those who have been educated, accounts for the majority. Many of them have graduated from middle school, and those with education account for about 70%. In addition, there is one thing that is also worth mentioning. The women in Guizhou Province are more motivated, thrifty, and hardworking than the men. Most of the men in the countryside sit at home and eat, are lazy to work, engage in jealousy, adultery, and fighting, and indulge in gambling, doing all kinds of evil. Since the establishment of the People's Militia, the village chiefs have forced the farmers to undergo military training and compulsory labor. Lazy men have to carry guns and walk more than ten or even dozens of miles early in the morning to assemble and train. In their spare time from farming, they also do various public works. As they have been used to this for a long time, the lazy have become diligent, and bad customs have been swept away. As a result, there are no beggars seeking food on the streets in the entire province. Those who are beggars are from other provinces. Guizhou has a vast territory and a sparse population and does not suffer from a lack of people to cultivate the land, but from a lack of cultivable land.

In recent years, Guizhou Province has paid close attention to the assimilation of the Yao ethnic group. It has repeatedly sent personnel to the Yao Mountains to promote and guide them, and the results have been good. The Yao people have also successively sent representatives to the province to discuss matters, and the assimilation work has been completed by 70-80%. There are 300,000 to 500,000 Yao people in Guizhou Province, with different languages and customs. Since the implementation of the People's Militia, the Guizhou authorities have also sent personnel to organize them in the Yao areas, giving them the same training. The village chiefs are entirely filled by Yao intellectuals, and they use this to promote basic national education, teaching them the Chinese language. It is heard that the land in the Yao Mountains is fertile and the products are very rich. The people are brave and good at climbing mountains. Assimilation and cooperation will have unlimited development prospects. According to the Guizhou authorities, in the past, the Yao and Miao ethnic groups hated the Han people very much. The reason was that the Han people bullied and oppressed the Yao and Miao due to their low level of knowledge, and the Han officials helped them to exploit them, forming a strong hatred for the Han people. Now that we treat them with kindness, show them the common interests, and provide equal treatment, they will naturally change their hatred into affection. The true foundation of the unity of the five ethnic groups lies here.

Yellow River Dike Closing Project - Construction of a Narrow-Gauge Railway from Liuhe to Dongzhuang - Actively Extending the Jiangsu Dike to Dig a Diversion Channel - The Eleven Provisions for Closing the Dike have been Largely Finalized 85

Jinan Correspondence: Kong Xiangrong, member of the Economic Commission and supervisor of the Yellow River flood control affairs in Hebei and Henan, advocated extending the Jiangsu Dike, diverting the water to correct the river course, and excavating a diversion channel to reduce the amount of water at the breach, making it easier to close. In addition, he also advocated building a narrow-gauge railway to transport materials. The day before yesterday, he came to Jinan from Kaifeng and exchanged views with Han Fuqu, chairman of the provincial government, and Zhang Honglie, director of the Construction Department and member of the Dike Closing Committee. They have largely reached an agreement. Today (7th) at about 9:00 AM, Zhang Honglie visited Kong at the Shitaiyan Hotel to make a final decision. It is planned to connect the northern end of the Jiangsu Dike to the embankment and build a stone dike to the Li Shengtun Embankment, extending it by 300 zhang in total, requiring an estimated 20,000 square feet of stone. At the same time, a diversion channel will be excavated, starting from the west of Li Shengtun Village to Zhangqiao, with a total length of 6.5 kilometers, a bottom width of 70 meters, and a mouth width of 120 meters. As for the transportation of materials, the original plan was to use the narrow-gauge railway from Lanfeng to Dongbatou, which has now been built. Stone materials can be transported by boat from Lanfeng to Dongbatou and then to Dongzhuang. However, a large amount of materials is needed, and it will take four months to transport them all on this narrow-gauge railway alone. Now it is planned to build another narrow-gauge railway, starting from the Liuhe Station on the Longhai Railway and going directly to the Dongzhuang opening via Heze, with a total length of 200 li. It would be much more convenient to transport materials by both railways. It is estimated that it will take one month to lay the railway and another month to transport all the stone materials. Regarding the materials needed for the 200-li railway, Zhang Honglie has discussed borrowing old materials from the Jiaoji Railway with Lu Mengxiong, a member of the railway committee. Lu has agreed to report to the railway authorities for consultation. Ge Guangting, chairman of the railway committee, will arrive in Jinan from Qingdao in the coming days, and Han will discuss the matter with him. If the railway authorities agree (the railway has enough track materials to lay 500 li), he will report to the Ministry of Railways for instructions. The Dike Closing Committee is working actively to raise funds for closing the dike opening. The engineering team decided to move to Dongzhuang. At the same time, a material factory will be set up in Dongzhuang. Zhou Li, director of the engineering team, Song Wentian, chief engineer, Yu Haomin, director of the material factory, Pan Yifen, chief of the engineering section of the River Affairs Bureau, Li Shilin, chief clerk, and engineers will depart by car tomorrow (8th) at 7:00 PM. The surveying team will also go with them. The party of 50 employees will travel in three long-distance buses and is scheduled to stay overnight in Taochengbu and arrive at their destination the next day. They are scheduled to stay in Dongzhuang for three weeks, but if the time is not enough, they may extend it for another week. Kong Xiangrong is in Jinan to discuss with Han Fuqu, chairman of the provincial government, and the Dike Closing Committee about dike closing, transportation of materials, and protection of Zhukou. A decision has been made, which can be roughly divided into eleven points: 1. Build a diversion dike behind the Jiangsu Dike to divert the water and correct the river course, reduce the flow of water from the breach, and provide relief to the disaster area. 2. The stone materials borrowed from Lanfeng and transported from Baimashan to Lanfeng will be transported to Dongbatou as soon as possible and shipped to the Dongzhuang construction site for use within a few days. 3. The Dike Closing Committee will send personnel to Huangzhuang to prepare for surveying and start construction immediately. 4. The amount of stone materials required for closing the breach is very large, and transportation is difficult. We will actively discuss building a 200-li railway from Lanfeng or Liuhe directly to Dongzhuang for convenient transportation. 5. Before the railway is successfully negotiated and built, we will first expedite the construction of the section of railway from Lanfeng to Dongbatou, about 20 li, and continue the shipping as a temporary means of transportation. 6. We will immediately send personnel to concentrate the borrowed narrow-gauge railway tracks and continue connecting them to supplement the transportation of materials. 7. We will send personnel to the Pinghan, Jinpu, and Jiaoji railways to negotiate for the allocation of vehicles, and negotiate with Longhai for the transportation of Taihushan stones, and ask the Pinghan Railway to allow the purchase of stone materials at Heshangqiao and Luwangfen. 8. Regarding the diversion channel decided to be excavated at the Dongzhuang meeting, we have sent personnel to survey it. As soon as the survey is completed, we will invite bids for construction. 9. At a suitable location on the Jiangsu Dike, we will extend the dike body to divert the flow, consolidate the Jiangsu Dike, and wash away the silt on the opposite bank to guide the flow into the correct course. We plan to investigate the water situation in the coming days and handle it accordingly. 10. Although the Zhukou dangerous project has been rescued and is now stable, for the sake of consolidation, we plan to consolidate the dike section and extend the stone dike at the end of Liuzhuang as a diversion shield. We plan to allocate part of the stone materials transported to Lanfeng to extend the dike. In addition to the 10,000 yuan of flood control funds allocated by Huang Lihui of the Supervision Department from the central government, it is heard that Chairman Han has also allocated 20,000 yuan for disaster relief, which has been handed over to Zhang Lianjia, director of the River Affairs Bureau, to purchase materials and carry out emergency repairs to prevent autumn floods. 11. Continue to expedite the consolidation of the Dongba base at the east end of the dike closure to prepare for the future closing. It is heard that Kong Xiangrong will stay in Jinan for a few days to discuss everything further. (7th)

A Sensation in Bingzhou: The Truth of the Bribery Case; Yan Xishan Advocates Strict Handling; The Inspection Committee Presents the Original Text to Yan 86

Jiading Pear Skin Causes Trouble Police Strike

At more than 5:00 p.m. on the 9th, Hu Xinggui, a shop assistant in the Yichangyong Towel Shop in front of the Pagoda in the city, discarded pear skin on the road. Chen Yangjie, a police trainee from the No. 26 post of the Zhouqiao Patrol, happened to be nearby. He saw the pear skin being thrown out and intervened with the shop. Hu immediately ordered an apprentice to pick it up. Officer Chen entered the shop and shouted accusations, and slapped the counter loudly. Zhu Quan, a shop assistant, protested, saying that slapping the counter was a taboo for merchants, and that the pear skin had already been picked up. Officer Chen immediately accused Zhu of being and detained Zhu. At that time, there were many who were tense in the street, and there was a lot of noise. During the disturbance, several window panes were broken. The shop immediately went up to the front door and stopped, and called the Public Security Bureau. The director (Chen Youmin) had been on leave for two weeks, and the clerk Zhu Cheng arrived at the scene, but had no solution, and immediately returned to the bureau. Since the above news came out, the crowd gathered in front of the tower with about a thousand people. There were four police trainees, including Zhuo Dengwen, in front of the pagoda, who were beaten. After being persuaded, they were led to Mingyuan Bathhouse to avoid the crowd. The county government heard the news and sent a security team to the scene, secretly deployed from Zhouqiao to Zhangma Lane, restricting pedestrians from standing. On the one hand, Captain Deng persuaded Officer Chen in the Yichangyong shop to return to the bureau. It was late at night, and the onlookers gradually dispersed. Outside the west gate, a police trainee was walking by the Diaoqiao pier, and a Taiyuan colleague Xu Xingsheng said that the police trainee was returning in disappointment, and was detained by the police and taken to the west gate branch. Patrol Chief Wang Cunhou reported to the county bureau, and the bureau ordered Xu to be sent to court. Hundreds of people went to the branch to inquire about the news. After mediation and bail, the crowd dispersed. The county public security office, believing that the police trainees had been beaten, sent five people, including Zhuo Dengwen, Chen Yangjie, Chen Zhiqiang, Liu Haiyi, and Huang Xiwu, to the county for examination of injuries that night. After the examination, Zhuo Dengwen was sent to Jiading Hospital for treatment. It was said that the injuries were still minor. The police trainees believed that they had a proper solution. On the 10th, all the police trainees inside and outside the city went on strike, and there were no police trainees stationed in the patrol posts.

Wuxi

Party and Government Handling of Zhenxin Workers' Unrest

Due to the accumulation of wages owed to employees by the Zhenxin Yarn Factory outside the west gate, a huge unrest occurred. Workers and staff members had repeatedly petitioned the county party headquarters, the county government, and the chamber of commerce. However, because the factory's associate managers Jiang Shiqing and Rong Xuxin were living in Shanghai to avoid the situation, and no one was in charge, there was no solution. On the morning of the 9th, more than 100 workers' representatives, including Wu Ada, Wu Borong, and Mi Fumei, petitioned the county government, requesting that the factory be ordered to resume work as soon as possible, and that the back wages and savings, etc., be paid off as soon as possible. At that time, County Magistrate Wang, together with Li Tiping, a member of the Standing Committee of the County Party Headquarters, and Qian Sunqing of the Chamber of Commerce, sent a quick letter to Jiang Zheqing, urging him to return to Wuxi immediately to take charge of the matter, so as to avoid the expansion of the unrest. Recently, Jiang's reply was received. Regarding the notice of suspension of work on August 1 and the resumption of work one month later, it was said that it had not been issued, but was posted by someone from the Party Headquarters and the Chamber of Commerce who guaranteed the cost, and there was no need for him to be responsible. Moreover, it pointed out that the unrest on July 31 was a case of gathering crowds, using violence, and coercion, and that if it was necessary to file a lawsuit in court, it would be easy to punish. It also requested that the handling methods for the suspension of work unrest in the Huafeng Flour Mill in Shanghai last month be followed. According to the letter, County Magistrate Wang and others, on the afternoon of the 10th, together with Party Committee Member Li Tiping, Sun Xiang, Xu Chizi, and Qian Sunqing of the Chamber of Commerce, etc., earnestly consulted at the Chamber of Commerce, believing that the factory's unrest had indeed expanded, and that if a quick solution was not used, there would never be a solution. According to the Company Law, for limited liability companies, all directors and supervisors should bear joint responsibility. After consultation, a strict solution was carried out. The county party headquarters also telegraphed the handling process to the central government and the two provincial regions yesterday, requesting clear instructions and hoping for a quick solution.

Local News

Hurricane Sweeps Shanghai and Attacks Korea; The "Haishang" Steamer Suffers Huge Losses; Other Ships Luckily Take Shelter Mid-Journey and Are All Safe 87

On the 7th of this month, a hurricane occurred at sea. Although it did not hit Shanghai, many merchant ships encountered the storm en route, causing delays. For example, the China Merchants Bureau's Taishun Steamer took shelter at 126 degrees 30 minutes east longitude and 33 degrees 36 minutes north latitude. After 24 hours, it was able to set sail yesterday. The Yushun Steamer also encountered the storm en route and telegraphed Shanghai yesterday, saying that it had safely arrived in Fuzhou. There was also the Jardine Matheson Northern Shipping Line's Dingsheng, which was delayed by one day due to the hurricane. The Dollar Steamship Line's ocean liner President Johnson, which came to Shanghai from Japan, was delayed by 36 hours due to taking shelter from the hurricane, and only entered port yesterday. Others who were delayed have all arrived in Shanghai one after another yesterday. However, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haishang steamer suffered the most damage, with its cabin surfaces damaged by the hurricane in the Korean seas. The details are as follows:

Loading Cargo in Korea

The Haishang steamer has a deadweight of 3,302 tons. It was previously leased to the government-run China Merchants Bureau to operate on the South China route. After the lease expired, it was leased to others to operate on the Kobe-Korea route. On the afternoon of the 7th of this month, the ship was loading cargo in Korea and was about to set sail for Japan when it was hit by a hurricane.

Damage from the Storm

The Haishang steamer was anchored in Korean waters, right in the center of the hurricane. The violent winds and waves were like mountains falling and seas overturning. The four rooms on the cabin surface, where the chief and second engineers and other crew members lived, were all destroyed. The iron railings on the upper deck were also broken off by the hurricane. A lifeboat was also blown away by the strong winds and waves and swept into the sea, its whereabouts unknown. The large iron anchor at the front of the ship fell into the water due to the breaking of the iron chain. The perilous situation made people yesterday.

Report to Shanghai

Yesterday afternoon, the shipowner telegraphed Shanghai to report to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, saying that the front of the cabin surface was all destroyed, and the Gangway Spors were also damaged. Fortunately, the hull was not damaged, and the entire crew fought against the fierce winds and waves to avoid injuries. Upon receiving the news, the company, in addition to reporting the situation to the insurance company, immediately telegraphed back, ordering a detailed report of all the damage caused by the hurricane, and ordered the ship to sail to Japan to find a way to repair the damaged areas, replace the new anchor, rebuild the cabins, and add lifeboats, etc., in order to restore its sailing power.

Australian Commissioner Arrives in Shanghai This Morning; Commissioner's Office to Be Established in Shanghai 90

Since its Deputy Prime Minister and Foreign Minister, Lanshan, visited various countries in the Far East, the British Australian government has decided to set up commercial commissioners in China, Japan, and the Dutch East Indies respectively. Bowden, the commercial commissioner assigned to China, and his assistant commissioner, Lette, arrived in Shanghai by the "Nanking" yesterday and stayed at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund. His commissioner's office is scheduled to be established in Shanghai. Bowden has lived in Shanghai for many years and is the general manager of A Cameron Compong, so he is very familiar with the commercial situation in China. Bowden told visiting reporters that the reason why the Australian government wants to set up a commercial commissioner in China is that it intends to develop Sino-Australian commerce and promote closer ties between the two countries. After taking office, he will do his best to make Sino-Australian relations closer and closer. It is also learned that its commercial commissioners stationed in Japan and the Dutch East Indies have also been assigned to Mr. Lauder, that is, Mr. Kregi Lai.

The "China Press" reported that Mr. Borden, the Australian Commercial Commissioner in China, arrived in Shanghai on the morning of the 9th after leaving Shanghai for six months, accompanied by Mr. Lutter, the Deputy Commercial Commissioner, on the Nanjing mail ship from Melbourne. Before taking up his current position, Mr. Borden had been doing business in Shanghai for many years, so he is familiar with the local business situation and has extensive contacts. In the future, he will travel to various commercial ports in China on a regular basis. According to Mr. Borden, the main purpose of the Australian government in appointing a commercial commissioner is to promote the sales of Australian products. His task includes collecting and disseminating information beneficial to this and to Australian merchants. Mr. Borden believes that good faith is an important factor if commercial ties are to develop to a satisfactory level. Therefore, he said that he will do his best to cultivate and expand the existing friendly relations between the Chinese and Australian business communities. During his recent visit to Australia, he traveled to several states and learned that Australian producers and merchants are very concerned about the expansion of commercial relations between China and Australia. All parties have promised to cooperate and assist, and the Australian government's Department of Commerce is particularly concerned about trade in the Far East. Australia's situation is getting better and better, the government's finances are very stable, and industry and commerce have made good progress. Australia's position today is far better than that of many other countries affected by the recession. He is willing to be in constant contact with those involved in the import trade of Australian products and will provide them with all possible information. Mr. Borden's current temporary residence is the Cathay Hotel, which will be used as an office until a suitable place is found.
