Spring and Autumn

Odds and Ends 135

— (Wang Shaba)

In the past, the union of men and women was combined under the feudal system's "parents' orders and matchmaker's words," leaving no room for one's own decisions. Consequently, both men and women, finding themselves incompatible, endured unspeakable suffering. In recent years, both men and women advocate "free love"—in theory, reducing all suffering. However, facts tell us otherwise. After marriage, there are countless disagreements, even leading to "divorce lawsuits," ending in separation. From this, we can realize that "free love is not necessarily blissful."

No matter how loving and understanding a couple may be, they sometimes turn against each other and quarrel for a while. Regarding this issue, I remember that when this newspaper's local news column held a "Reader's Mailbox" three years ago, a certain gentleman offered this explanation: "The bickering in a marriage is like the winding of a clock's spring, an inevitable stage. The spring of a clock, after running for a while, must be unwound and then rewound before it can run again. A couple is the same: a quarrel is like winding the spring." This is truly a wonderful analogy.

Upside-Down Clothing 136

— Zheng Yimei

The ancients clearly distinguished between the two characters for clothing, calling it: "The upper garment is called 'yi,' the lower garment is called 'chang.'" Therefore, shirts, vests, and jackets belong to the "yi" category. Trousers, socks, and skirts belong to the "chang" category. Even women in old families clearly distinguished between upper and lower garments, and the washing of clothes had separate tubs for upper and lower body garments. Even the bamboo poles for drying clothes, those designated for upper garments, were exclusively used for upper garments. When hiring a new maid, it was necessary to repeatedly remind them, "This is for the upper body, this is for the lower body," allowing no confusion. Ever since the social atmosphere changed drastically, and modern fashion was admired, the boundaries between upper and lower body were broken, and outdated lower garments were slightly altered and brought to the upper body. The first example is leggings. Leggings have trouser legs but no crotch, making them simpler to make. Furthermore, silk leggings were prepared to cover up the crudeness of cloth trousers. This was also where the elders showed their cleverness. Unexpectedly, these leggings have long been eliminated, but we now see police officers on the streets with sleeves on their elbows. Comedians say, "This is a disguised form of leggings, suddenly transforming from the lower body to the upper body." Coming to the present day, women are increasingly going barefoot, wearing openwork leather shoes, strolling through the city. Urban people are accustomed to this sight and no longer find it strange. According to a modern woman who spoke to me, "This barefoot trend is purely for economic reasons. It's because a pair of silk stockings, costing several yuan, wears out so quickly that it's better to go barefoot directly. People think going barefoot is so cool, but they don't know we're suffering. Because socks absorb sweat, without socks, the sweat makes our feet slippery and uncomfortable, especially for those of us who like to dance. After dancing several times, blisters easily form on our feet, causing pain that's hard to express." I said, "Since you're talking about economics, then why save on socks but wear gloves in such hot weather? Isn't that moving the lower body's socks to the upper body?" That modern woman glared at me with almond-shaped eyes and said, "You're clearly scolding me, but the cost of gloves is much cheaper than socks."

Selling Flowers 137

— Zhu Ying

In our alley, every morning between seven and seven-thirty, a fifteen-year-old Suzhou girl comes to sell fresh flowers. (Not white orchids, but fresh flowers for inserting into vases.) Although she is not beautiful, she is petite and exquisite, and her slightly charming, half-innocent naiveté is indeed somewhat pleasing. Therefore, every morning when she comes, among the thirty-odd tenants in our apartment, at least a third of them use buying a bunch of fresh flowers as an excuse to chat idly with her, pestering her. I am a vulgar person, fundamentally ignorant of the art of appreciating flowers, and I also lack the leisure to flirt with that girl, so I originally didn't want to buy any. However, those room attendants almost had to come and peddle flowers to me for that girl every day. Sometimes, unable to resist, I would spend a dozen or so coppers to buy a bunch and use the pen holder as a vase to display them.

Last week, for a whole week, the room attendants didn't come to bother me, which I found very strange. Yesterday, I had to go out early, and as I walked downstairs, I suddenly saw two room attendants pushing an old flower-selling woman out the door. The old woman was struggling and pleading bitterly. I felt strange and hurriedly asked what was happening. The old woman said, "My daughter used to sell more than half a dollar's worth of fresh flowers here every morning. These past few days, she suddenly fell ill, and when I came to sell, these two gentlemen wouldn't let me in. Alas, sir, we are poor people, and if we can't do business, we will have nothing to eat. I beg you, sir, to please be accommodating." As she spoke, tears rolled down her face. But those two room attendants fiercely shouted, "Old woman, get out of here! Who wants to buy your old woman's flowers?"

Pleasure Village? 138

— Jiang Mi

The Blind 139

— Han Yu

On the roads and in the lanes, one can often hear the clanging of iron plates, which shows how many blind people there are.

Blind people are indeed pitiful, unable to see things and unable to do things. But the whip of life also strikes heavily on their backs, forcing them to find ways to support themselves.

Fortune-telling is the biggest outlet for blind people, but it is more difficult for them to learn, as they have to memorize everything. After learning, some open shops, like the "Direct Talk Fortune-Telling" shops that line Xizang Road. Their main business is not fortune-telling, but rather helping those who do fortune-telling to do penance. Their clever mouths can explain how bad the fleeting years are, making people willingly take out money. Another type is those who clang iron plates. They are often supported by someone. Their income is not very plentiful, because there is no extra income.

Character divination is also a profession for blind people. They dig several different holes on each character card. As long as they feel the number of holes, they know what character it is. The last type is beggars. They simply have no ability to be self-reliant and can only use their disabilities as tools for begging.

Blind people are indeed pitiful, and there are many people who pity them; therefore, there are many who are not blind but pretend to be blind to make a living. There is a blind fortune-teller in Nicheng Bridge who, although he keeps his eyes closed, his eyeballs are constantly moving. After a few minutes, he must open his eyes to feel comfortable. Once, he was buying cigarettes with his eyes open, and people laughed at him, and he couldn't help but laugh himself.

Blind people must have someone to help them when walking on the road. Therefore, most blind beggars are fake.

Local Customs

Newsreel 140

— Shanghai General News Agency

The world's ears and eyes: cameras, film, and screens, combined to dominate the throne of current affairs reports in the new century.

In June 1921, the 5th Far Eastern Games were held at Hongkou Park in Shanghai. The Commercial Press Motion Picture Department, with the consent of the association, collaborated with Dr. Peter, director of the YMCA film department, to film newsreels on-site, totaling three reels: the first reel was the scene of athletes entering the stadium and the opening ceremony, the second reel was the finals of various sports, and the third reel was the girls' gymnastics and the Boy Scout exercises. These three reels initiated the production of Chinese newsreels.

Mingxing Film Company occupies the position of the elder brother in the Chinese film industry because it was established earlier and still survives to this day. Do you remember what its debut film was? "The Orphan's Rescue" perhaps you might answer. But its first official film, not its first production. "Then, is it 'The Adventures of the King of Comedy in Shanghai'?" No, Mingxing Company's production did not start with a comedy, but with a newsreel: On March 9, 1922, French General Joffre came to Shanghai for sightseeing. He was the general who became famous for saving France from danger in the Battle of the Marne during the European War. The French Concession in Shanghai renamed the most prosperous Baochang Road to Joffre Road in 1915 to express gratitude. At this time, Joffre visited Shanghai, and Joffre Road was decorated with lights to welcome him, which was very grand. It was at this time that Mingxing Film Company was organized and established, and it filmed the scene of welcoming General Joffre as a test film. This test film was premiered at the YMCA in early April, while "The Adventures of the King of Comedy in Shanghai" was premiered at the Xia Ling Pei Ke Grand Theater on August 15 of the same year, and "The Orphan's Rescue" was premiered at the Shenjiang Grand Theater in December of the following year.

Although newsreels were produced in 1921-22, their importance had not yet been noticed, so occasional productions were made, but they did not develop. They only became slightly popular after 1927.

In 1930, Lianhua Film Company was established and paid much attention to the production of newsreels, publishing an issue every month on average, called "Lianhua News." By May 1933, a total of 30 issues had been published. At that time, the Propaganda Committee of the Central Party Department, in view of the great power of newsreels to convey current events, specially ordered the film division of the Central Propaganda Committee and Lianhua Company to cooperate in the production of newsreels. Previously, the Central Propaganda Committee also had newsreels published, which had reached 10 issues. After the cooperation, it assisted Lianhua in sending personnel to various places to film news, expanding the scope and enriching the materials, and renamed it "China News," with the signature "Jointly produced by the Propaganda Committee of the Central Committee and Lianhua Film Company." A total of 45 issues were published in a year. Previously, each issue only contained one current event, but now it contained at least three recent current events, and at most nine. In May of the following year, the one-year contract signed by both parties expired and was not renewed. In November, the film division of the Central Propaganda Committee was expanded into a film section and rebuilt into the Central Film Studio. Both parties continued to produce newsreels separately.

The production of Chinese newsreels, whether in quality or quantity, is far behind Europe and the United States; but compared to the past, it has improved a lot. I wish it continued progress! I especially hope that the news media and the film industry will cooperate, like Hearst and MGM in the United States, and the crystallization of the two companies will truly be a "newsreel"!

Xiaoxitian (Little Western Paradise) 141

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: Qi Party's High-Climbing Flattery Reprimands Minor Officials, Female Power Rises Greatly, Noisy Troubles the Madam

Jia Duocai gently shouted, "You've only been here for a few days, and you already want to go back. If that's the case, your family shouldn't have sold you." After speaking, he gently tapped the table again. This was followed by the sound of Yueying sniffing and the sobbing becoming slightly softer. Ma San felt it was an opportunity to speak and quietly walked to the door, saying through the curtain, "Madam Jia, you really can't cry anymore. Commissioner Gai upstairs has lost his temper and is only asking who is crying. He says that if you cry again, he will drive you off the mountain." Jia Duocai said, "What? Drive me out? You come in and talk." Ma San couldn't have been happier and walked in. He saw Jia Duocai sitting by the table with his head held high, smoking a cigarette. Yueying was sitting in the corner of the bed, sobbing and weeping incessantly. Jia Duocai said, "I am a businessman, whether it's a commissioner or an official, he can't control me. How can he say he wants to drive me out?" Ma San, seeing his attitude was so tough, pursed his lips and said, "Look at this bad luck! I got beaten up for your wife's crying." He described the incident of going upstairs, exaggerating it. Jia Duocai slammed the table and shouted, "This is outrageous! Xiaoxitian is not something I rented alone, nor is it something that Old Commissioner Gai rented alone. He can do whatever he wants in Xiaoxitian, but can't we cry in our own room? People are sad and shed tears, crying is inevitable. Given his status, when someone is crying, he should investigate what grievances they have suffered. How can he say that people are disturbing him? We insist on crying, let's see what he does to me!" (312)

The Fragrant Shadow of the Imperial Incense 142

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Besides applying egg white every night to prevent the wrinkles on her face from continuing to lengthen or expand, the Empress Dowager also had many methods specifically for dealing with those wrinkles. One of them was very special. Originally, there were two jade sticks, about two or three inches long, with gold handles at both ends, installed on her dressing table. Every morning, she had to use them to roll up and down on her face. This thing was very smooth and cold, and there was no powder applied to it, so I really didn't know what its function was? The Empress Dowager always sat patiently in front of the dressing table, constantly rolling it on her face, staring intently at the mirror, as if rolling it a few times would have an immediate effect. I was very surprised. Once, when she was not around, I boldly picked up a jade stick and tried it for a while. Unexpectedly, the Empress Dowager happened to walk in and was very unhappy when she saw it. But her unhappiness was not because I secretly used her old lady's things, but because she knew that I had some doubts about the function of her jade stick, so she was unhappy.

"This thing is of no use to you!" She immediately spoke very seriously, "People as young as you don't need any egg white, pearl powder, fat oil, etc.! This kind of jade stick is even more unnecessary!"

"Please forgive me, Empress Dowager!" I hurriedly kowtowed to her and apologized, "This servant did not dare to secretly use the Empress Dowager's things indiscriminately, but I just thought this jade stick was so smooth and cute, and I wanted to try it to see how comfortable it would be to roll on the skin... But I will definitely not dare to do it again next time!"

National Games Organizing Committee Announces Registration Methods for Journalists; Registration Begins Immediately and Closes at the End of the Month; Location: Mainland Marketplace, Room 306 151

The registration methods for journalists for the 6th National Games have been submitted to and approved by the 10th Standing Committee Meeting of the Organizing Committee for implementation. The full text of the registration methods is listed below. The registration location is located inside Room 106 of the Mainland Marketplace on Nanjing Road, Shanghai, as it is more accessible for transportation. The registration methods for journalists for the 6th National Games are listed as follows:

(1) All national newspapers and news agencies wishing to send reporters to cover the news of the Games must register with the Organizing Committee from now until September 30th (inside Room 206 of the Mainland Marketplace on Nanjing Road, Shanghai).

(2) When journalists register with the Organizing Committee, they must submit a certificate of authorization from the newspaper or news agency they serve, along with two 2.5-inch head-and-shoulder photographs, to the Organizing Committee for review. Upon approval, a registration card will be issued. This card will be used to enter the venue during the Games.

(3) When registering, journalists must fill out the registration form prescribed by the Organizing Committee (form attached separately).

(4) Special seating for journalists will be provided at each venue by the Organizing Committee. Each member newspaper of the Daily Newspaper Association and the Central News Agency will be limited to one seat per venue. The Organizing Committee's Propaganda Group, in conjunction with the Shanghai Municipal News Censorship Office, will manage this process, based on actual needs, for all Chinese and foreign newspapers and news agencies registered centrally with the Organizing Committee.

(5) During the competition, journalists are not allowed to enter the competition areas designated for athletes.

(6) All news releases from the Organizing Committee must be reviewed and stamped by the Propaganda Group before they can be sent out (in the case of private conversations, names must be published to indicate responsibility).

(7) Journalists are not allowed to talk to or photograph athletes during competition (methods for providing news photographs will be determined separately).

(8) Journalists wishing to investigate athletes' resumes must do so during athletes' rest periods.

(9) If a journalist violates the regulations of the Organizing Committee or any temporary announcements, the Propaganda Group of the Organizing Committee may revoke their registration card at any time.

(10) These methods are submitted to the Standing Committee for approval and implementation.

Municipal National Games Swimming Preliminaries Scheduled for the 16th; Springboard is Being Rushed for Repairs; First Diving Test This Week; Rules of Water Entry Competition Determined for This National Games 152

The municipal swimming mixed training has been underway since the 1st of this month and has already been tested three times. The final preliminary selection was originally scheduled to be held around the 10th. However, due to the damage to the springboard at the Sino-Youth swimming pool and the fact that the new springboard at the municipal pool has not yet been properly installed, the diving athletes have not yet been tested. Now, coach Peng Sanmei plans to hold the swimming preliminary selection on the afternoon of the 16th of this month (next Monday) to select the official swimming representatives for Shanghai City to attend the current National Games. As for the diving test, the Sino-Youth springboard is being actively rushed for repairs, and it is planned to hold the first test this week. In addition, the diving rules are extremely complex.

The Shanghai interport team participating in the Hong Kong-Shanghai interport swimming competition has decided to travel to Hong Kong on the morning of the 14th aboard the President Coolidge, which is leaving Shanghai. The team leader is Mr. Hex. The team is scheduled to board the ship at the New Customs Wharf at 11 PM on the 13th and arrive in Hong Kong on the 16th. The interport competition is scheduled to be held on the 19th, 20th, and 23rd at the Hong Kong Victoria Recreation Club. The Shanghai team is scheduled to return to Shanghai from Hong Kong by ship on the 25th and is expected to arrive around the 27th. This year, the Hong Kong team has five Chinese athletes: Chen Zhenxing, a renowned 50-yard and 100-yard freestyle swimmer; Guo Zhenheng, who will be coming to Shanghai to study and is skilled in breaststroke; Liu Baoxi, who is skilled in backstroke; Huang Xipei, who is a diving expert; and Chen Xipei. As for the strengths of the Shanghai and Hong Kong teams this year, there are high hopes for the 50-yard, 100-yard, and diving events. Chen Zhenxing's 50-yard time is 25.2 seconds, while the times of Shanghai's Heimond, Bretton, and Wood are all around 25 seconds. It is also said that the original representatives selected for the 50-yard event were Heimond and Bretton, but now, due to too many events, Wood has taken over. As for the 220-yard, 440-yard, and 880-yard events, Hong Kong has the great Trolis, whose 880-yard time is 11 minutes and 49 seconds, 440-yard time is 5 minutes and 35 seconds, and 220-yard time is 2 minutes and 25 seconds. In comparison, Shanghai's highest records are: Krek's 880-yard time is 12 minutes and 59 seconds, Heimond's 440-yard time is 5 minutes and 46 seconds, and 220-yard time is 2 minutes and 30 seconds. The difference is too great, and there is no hope. The team consists of ten people, and the list is as follows:

Roster

Open All Day Every Sunday 157

Since the Shanghai Municipal Swimming Pool opened on the 8th and was opened to the public on the 9th, people from all walks of life have been visiting and swimming in large numbers in recent days. In order to improve management and facilities, and to promote the public's interest in sports, the pool convened its first management meeting on the afternoon of the 10th. Attendees included Li Dachao, Yu Binqi, Qiu Songsheng, Yan Xuzhang, Wu Tiequn, Zhang Rongguang, Yuan Weitang, Meng Meng, and Chen Zuogan from Lianhua. Li Dachao chaired the meeting. During the meeting, there were detailed discussions on ticket sales, rental of bathrobes and keys, body inspections, and first aid, and it was decided that the pool will be open all day every Sunday from now on. Ticket sales will begin at 7 AM, and swimming hours will be from 8 AM to 11 AM and from 1 PM to 6 PM. On regular days, the pool will still be open from 2 PM to 6 PM.

Amazing Results in the Nanyang Cup Division B; Li Wei Unexpectedly Overwhelms Liu Jie; Rain Repeatedly Hinders the Tournament; Finals Date Changed to the 19th; Old Qiu's Mishap; Performance by Celebrated Western Players Might Not Happen 158

The Shanghai Lawn Tennis Association originally planned to hold the finals of the Nanyang Cup Division A, B and C tournaments simultaneously during the Mid-Autumn Festival and to invite celebrated Western tennis players to participate in an exhibition match to entertain guests. However, due to unexpected difficulties, it was necessary to make temporary changes. The details are described as follows:

Finals Date Changed to the 19th

Due to recent rain and wet courts, the matches have been hindered. Apart from Division C, the Committee has been actively trying to schedule make-up matches for Division A and B. However, due to the tardiness of a few players, the match schedules of other players in the same group have been affected. Therefore, the Committee has now decided that all players shall be allowed to complete the Division A and B semi-finals within six days from today (the 11th) to the 16th, so that the Committee will be able to schedule the finals of Division A, B and C on the afternoon of September 19th (Thursday) at 3 p.m.

Feihai Disappointed and Listless

The exhibition match was originally scheduled to have Mr. Qiu Feihai responsible for inviting Western friends. However, Mr. Qiu has been in poor form recently and in a bad mood. Yesterday, he suffered another defeat at the hands of Wang Wenzheng. As a result, he has not yet contacted any Western tennis players as of today, which makes it unlikely that the exhibition match will take place, dealing a blow to the perfect plans for the Nanyang Cup, which is also regrettable. In addition, Mr. Qiu has suffered repeated setbacks, returning defeated and crestfallen, his great ambitions have been diminished. As a result, his matches with Hou Shangxiong and Qian Yaobin have been postponed until today, affecting the overall situation.

Predictions for the Division B and C Champions

In Division B, Li Wei unexpectedly defeated Liu Zengshu by 6-3, 4-6, 6-4. If he can overcome Xu Demin in the semi-finals, then the hope of winning the championship will be as easy as turning his hand. In Division C, Chen Qihao and Zhan Wenyu fought fiercely for four sets in the semi-finals yesterday without being able to determine the winner. Today, they will have to continue the match. The winner will then face the winner of the match between Wang Shuqing and Zhou Jiaqi in the finals. In terms of skill, Mr. Wang seems to have the upper hand and is most likely to win the championship. However, Mr. Wang's father suddenly passed away yesterday, so he had to abandon his ambitions.

Outline of Methods for Training Labor Education Teachers in Provinces and Cities 164

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the Education Bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 9th, stating: It has been found that the National Vocational School and Primary School Labor Education Achievement Exhibition held in the 23rd year of this Union showed progress in the labor education works of primary schools in various regions. However, the selection and organization of teaching materials have not been fully in line with educational principles, and the local special raw materials have not been given enough attention. To achieve improvement, it is essential to train labor education teachers. The Ministry has formulated a temporary outline of methods for training primary school labor education teachers in various provinces and cities, which is attached herewith. You are instructed to comply with it, formulate an implementation plan, and submit it to the Ministry for approval. This order pertains to the temporary outline of methods for training primary school labor education teachers in various provinces and cities.

1. The education administrative authorities of each province and city shall designate a well-established normal school or vocational school to establish a labor education teacher training class according to the actual needs of the province or city.

2. The labor education teacher training class shall enroll graduates of three-year junior vocational schools, junior high schools, or old-system Category A industrial schools, or those with equivalent qualifications, and provide them with two to three years of training.

3. The labor education teacher training class shall enroll incumbent primary school labor education teachers with three or more years of labor education teaching experience and provide them with one to two years of training.

4. Those trained as labor education teachers may also study industry, agronomy, home economics, etc., with each person studying at least two types.

5. The normal or vocational schools designated to train primary school labor education teachers must have sufficient equipment in metalworking shops, woodworking shops, and agronomy and home economics practice sites.

6. In addition to referring to the subjects and hours of the special normal department, the subjects and time for study shall be allocated as follows: general subjects, 20% to 30%; education subjects and practice, 20%; labor subjects, 60%. For those with a training period of one year, the number of hours for general subjects may be appropriately reduced, and the number of hours for labor subjects may be increased.

7. The enrollment methods for designated normal or vocational schools shall be determined by the education administrative authorities of each county, based on actual needs, to send multiple candidates in batches to the school for re-examination. After graduation, the candidates shall be assigned to work by the original sending authority.

8. Tuition fees shall be waived, and living expenses shall be subsidized by the original sending authority as appropriate.

9. The education bureaus of each province and city shall formulate an implementation plan in accordance with this outline and submit it to the Ministry for approval.

Municipal Primary and Secondary Schools Universally Install Radios 166

#### The Education Bureau Has Conducted a Survey and Requested Approval from the Public Utilities Bureau, and Radio Broadcasts Can Begin Once the Municipal Radio Station is Established

The municipal government's radio station is about to be established, and the broadcasting review committee is also being organized. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau recently convened a meeting of bureau representatives to discuss the universal installation of radios. It was decided that all municipal middle schools must install one radio, and the Municipal Education Bureau will survey the municipal primary schools. Schools with six or more classes will install radios as needed. It is understood that the Municipal Education Bureau has completed the survey, totaling more than 40 radios in primary and secondary schools, and has sent a list to the Public Utilities Bureau for approval. Once the municipal government's radio station is established, radio broadcasts can begin. Radios are a powerful tool for promoting social education. After the station is established, schools can use radios to receive broadcasts related to education. As for private primary and secondary schools, the Education Bureau has previously forwarded the Ministry's order to each school for installation.

Liangjiang Enrolls Overseas Free Students 169

#### Already Assigned by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission

This time, the Liangjiang Women's Physical Education Normal School in this city has added 50 free student positions for poor students, 30 in China, selected and recommended by the education bureaus of each province and city, one from each province and city. The examination and recommendation of students from the three northeastern provinces and Rehe province is handled by the Northeast Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry of Education. For overseas Chinese students in Southeast Asia, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission will send letters to the consulates and the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce to select and recommend them. The association has carefully considered the situation of overseas Chinese in various parts of Southeast Asia and has allocated the places appropriately. Five places are allocated to British Malaya, four to Dutch East Indies, two to Siam, and one each to British North Borneo, Burma, Annam, and the Philippines. Notices have been sent to them to expedite the process. Liangjiang has received replies from the Philippines, Hebei, Hunan, and other places, stating that they have handled the matter in accordance with the regulations. In recent days, many people have written to the school to inquire about the methods of enrolling free students, and many have directly recommended students. The school has a limited number of places and is concerned that the procedures may be different and cannot be universally accepted, which is quite regrettable. However, for one overseas Chinese student recommended from Padang and Manado in Southeast Asia, Principal Lu has waived tuition fees and given preferential treatment in consideration of the difficulty of returning to China.

Little Men (42) 170

#### Original work by American Ms. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

One day, Ned poked his head into Mrs. Pei's room and said, "Teacher, I have something to tell you. Do you have time? This is a very important matter."

This was already the fifth head that had poked into the room in the last half hour; however, Mrs. Shu was used to it, so she raised her head and said briskly, "What is it, my child?"

Ned then walked in, carefully closed the door behind him, and said with a look of urgency, "Donn is here."

"Who is Donn?"

"He is a boy I know from playing the piano in the street. He sells newspapers and treats me very well. I saw him in town the other day and told him how good it is here, and now he is here."

"But, my child, it's too sudden for him to come as a guest."

"Ah, he's not here as a guest. He wants to live here, if you allow him!" Ned said innocently.

"Well, I don't know about that." Mrs. Pei replied, startled by the rash suggestion.

Most Shops and Businesses Close for the Mid-Autumn Festival 173

All Chinese and foreign banks, exchanges, money shops, silver shops, and commercial factories will be closed for one day as usual. The banks on the Bund will be closed as usual. Although the Gregorian calendar is now used, they could be open. However, since most silver and money businesses are closed, they have to follow suit.

Free Talk

Annals of the Gengzi Year from Abroad 186

— Han Feng

I once mentioned a Gengzi notebook titled "Annals of Yuguan," pointing out the mutual contradictions of imperialism in China at that time as reflected in that book. Recently, I acquired a four-volume "Annals of the Gengzi Year from Abroad." Initially, I only intended to look at the foreign situation during the Gengzi year, but I unexpectedly discovered the same characteristics as "Annals of Yuguan," allowing us to see more clearly how the "Allied Forces" were secretly fighting. Although the author is the German ambassador Lü Hai-mai, it is not exactly an "official document."

This book was compiled when Lü Hai-bao stepped down from his post in the Xin Chou year (1901) and returned to his home country to have it printed. It records everything from the beginning of the incident to Prince Chun representing the Qing court to Germany to offer apologies, and his own resignation. The first volume contains the telegrams he sent to the Chinese government, officials in various provinces, and ministers in other countries. The second volume contains telegrams from various parties. Volume three records his conversations each time he visited the Qing foreign minister. The last volume contains imperial edicts, treaties, German replies, and translated foreign opinions.

The "Preface" describes the situation in Germany at that time: "When the killing of the envoy led to conflict, and the Allied Forces invaded the north, Germany's precautions increased, resulting in secret telegrams. It was heard that they were delivered circuitously through other envoys, and information about Chinese affairs was often blocked, making it difficult to ascertain the truth, similar to ancient wax letters or messages tied to geese. When the news of Minister Ketteler's assassination reached Berlin, the whole country was in an uproar. Ignorant people often made disrespectful remarks towards the Chinese embassy. Therefore, I strictly instructed the staff and translators to stay indoors to avoid danger." This is a fact that we would expect. The telegrams he sent also generally confirm this. A telegram on July 9th stated: "The German envoy was killed, and the German Emperor is very angry. He has sent four ironclad ships and one speedboat to China, with about two thousand soldiers. He vows to take Beijing and form an alliance under the city walls. Public sentiment in Berlin is turbulent and the situation is very dangerous." However, a telegram on June 23rd already contained the words "Recently, rumors have become more malicious, and officials and civilians in the German capital are panicked. Various countries are conspiring against us," indicating that even before Ketteler was harmed, various countries were already communicating with each other and preparing for war.

The most amusing thing is that the Chinese government, even though Ketteler's death had become a well-known fact, still tried to cover it up, which is incredibly foolish. A telegram from the Beiyang Minister Li on June 5th stated: "… Minister's telegram, the German envoy was killed by rioters in the capital. No one outside knows. Secretly consider whether there are any measures to eliminate the problem." Such a major event was described as "no one outside knows," and asking "whether there are any measures to eliminate the problem" is simply absurd. But the absurdity doesn't stop there. Later, when going to Germany to offer apologies, the German Emperor insisted that Prince Chun and his entourage kowtow. After much negotiation, the German Emperor only allowed Prince Chun to be exempted. What were Prince Chun's plans at this time? A telegram on July 19th stated: "However, the counselors kneeling and bowing would harm the national dignity. Now, as a compromise, only bring Jin Kai and Geng Yin-tai as interpreters when delivering the letter of credence. Zhang Yin-chang and others should still follow the previous telegram, either feigning illness or temporarily avoiding the scene, to avoid kneeling and being humiliated." It is truly unexpected how pathetic and laughable this is. This is why the German Emperor finally conceded, insisting that the letter of credence must be "received while seated."

Where is the so-called reflection of the contradictions between imperialist powers? On August 13th of the Gengzi year, the minister to Russia sent a telegram stating: "The culprits have been punished, and compensation has been paid for the killing of the envoy. The German commander has not been allowed to come to Tianjin, and German troops have been dispatched to Jinghai, while Russian troops have been dispatched to seize the Beizhi and the Taishan Customs. What is the conspiracy?" The "What is the conspiracy?" doesn't need to be asked. The "Annals of Yuguan" has already indicated it directly: Russia wants to open a route back home, occupying the important roads to Russia. Germany, England, and others fear that they will gain an advantage, so they take advantage of the Russian troops' movements to occupy the Jian Pass area with their navy. The same can be seen in the "Annals of the Gengzi Year from Abroad." The death of Waldersee should have been an important matter for Germany, but from the repeated conversations between the German foreign minister and Ambassador Lü, it does not seem to be the focus. What is the focus? It is actually the actions of countries other than Germany in China. Has China given them special benefits? Have they signed secret agreements with other countries granting them special commercial interests? For example, a telegram on January 3rd of the Xin Chou year stated: "The Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent a letter requesting a meeting, stating that before the peace talks are concluded, China should not sign agreements with them or their companies, ceding land, money, and other benefits." A telegram on the 4th stated: "I suspect that Germany fears that other countries will take the opportunity to seize benefits. They are now the leader of the Allied Forces and cannot help but think about gaining benefits, but they do not want to be criticized." A telegram on March 11th is even more mysterious:

Yesterday, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs secretly stated: Whether the Allied Forces withdraw depends on the payment of reparations. It is heard that Governor Zou is very anxious about the payment of reparations. If there is a practical solution, it may be confidentially informed. If the matter is feasible, Germany will definitely make extra concessions and help China persuade other countries to agree. Please relay this message confidentially to the Xiang Governor." I have already sent a confidential telegram to the Xiang Governor. When asked about their intentions, they secretly said that they heard that some people were profiting from the payment of reparations, and they feared that Chinese officials would be deceived by them. Therefore, Germany wanted to know China's true intentions. Please keep it secret to prevent disclosure.

This truly reveals the so-called "Sima Zhao's intention," such as "Germany will definitely make extra concessions!" The book also records many questions from the German Foreign Ministry: Is the news of the agreement with a certain country true? What kind of benefits have been given to that country? They constantly criticize that all countries have bad intentions, "only Germany can help China." Those who heard these sweet words at the time must have had certain feelings. In fact, all crows under the sky are equally black, further exposing the reality of their mutual contradictions. This is revealed in telegrams and conversations, and I will not list more examples. It says very little about the domestic situation, mainly focusing on the interactions between the minister and Germany. The translated articles attached at the end of the book include some that express goodwill towards China and others that attack it, but none of them can see a bit of "justice" like the few articles excerpted in the "Selections of Humor and Seriousness." Therefore, I will abandon this and quote seven excerpts from the "Selections":

A French military officer said: "The intention of the Boxers is very good. Chinese people should deceive all foreign missionaries who want to come to China to preach. If I were a Chinese, I would want to do what the Chinese do. If China wants to preach to our France, I would also want to drive them out of France." A certain newspaper in England wrote about the Boxers: "We thought China was completely dead, but now there are these people, so it is not completely dead!" Count Okuma of Japan said: "Do not criticize the Boxers. What we did thirty years ago was also like the Boxers." A German soldier who returned home spoke highly of the Boxers: "Children over ten years old can all hold knives and move forward, not afraid of death at all. Even if the front row is dead, they continue to advance. They are truly incredibly brave." He also said: "German soldiers once fought in a certain place and saw soldiers fall down. They then drove forward, and the fallen soldiers suddenly rose up, killing dozens of people. Another German soldier who was transferred back to the country from China said in Nagasaki that the military officer to the Yang Bank said: 'Chinese soldiers are said to be useless, but in fact, they are not. Their bravery is unmatched by Western soldiers. I fought with Chinese soldiers in Tianjin. One Chinese soldier had already suffered seven injuries, but he still fought bravely forward. Finally, he was hit in the foot and fell down. I thought he was dead. Our soldiers drove past him, but unexpectedly, the soldier suddenly got up and desperately grabbed my soldier's foot. My soldier looked at his face, which was covered in blood and flesh, and was terrified, almost dying with him. Later, he stabbed him with the knife on the tip of his gun, and he fell down again. My soldier was able to escape.'"

These opinions are truly credible, but unfortunately, very few people know them. Now, I am fortunate to have encountered them, allowing us to glimpse the heroism of the Boxers, which is completely different from the general records and rumors. The "Selections of Humor and Seriousness" also discusses the "Boxer bandits," saying: "It is not known that although the Boxer affair cannot be taken as a lesson, its intention is quite surprising to Europeans. For decades, Europeans have insulted our people, and even bystanders cannot bear it. But none of the Chinese ministers have destroyed their families to face the national crisis, and none of the minor officials have united to fight for national justice. At that time, scholars were all immersed in personal gain. Now, suddenly someone rises up out of anger, not afraid of death, not avoiding difficulties. They believe that China still has vitality, or perhaps that China will revive because of this. All those in our country who have a little vitality must know this." This is a very insightful statement. I do not know who said it. However, it can also be seen from this that it is not necessary to wait until today to make a fair assessment of the Boxer Rebellion. Because I am discussing the "Annals of the Gengzi Year from Abroad," I have specially included this.

The Return Journey 187

— Jiang Ji-ping

This morning, there was indeed a hint of autumn coolness. Although not all the leaves have fallen, the coolness of early autumn is already enough to make people uncomfortable. While I was still in bed, I heard the wind outside the window sounding a bit different. I aimlessly chanted, "The autumn wind rises, white clouds fly; the grass and trees turn yellow, geese fly south," and felt a bit sad in my heart. After getting up and opening the curtains, the sun was still so intimidating that my sadness disappeared again. In the evening, as I passed the front of the garden, the leaves of the poplar trees rustled. Suddenly, I remembered the line from an ancient poem, "Why are the poplars so rustling?" I looked up and saw that the leaves were still very dense, a dark green that was almost frightening. Perhaps because the sky was getting dark, the leaves of the trees were completely black. I felt uncomfortable again and lowered my head, afraid to look at it.

When I usually walk with my head down, I always think silently, so sometimes I even bump into people. After apologizing to them, I find it amusing. This habit of pondering is not good, I know it myself; but what can I do to stop it from thinking? My brain is not under my control, and besides, I have so many memories? For example, when the leaves of the poplar trees rustle, I think of something. Two years ago, I sat under a tree with a lady. Now we are married and have children. At that time, we were planning our future happiness and the brightness of our future, but what about now? Everything has disappeared, everything is mediocre. I don't know what path I should be walking. I only feel that people in this world are just "drifting"! The ancients said, "Life is like a floating dream," "Time flies like a swift horse passing a crack," and "My life is truly like floating." We seem to sigh too often about how quickly time passes, but the children who used to play ball with me have already gotten married. What can we do to not sigh about the rapid passage of time?

Looking up again, the crescent moon is already hanging on the corner of the pavilion. In a few days, it will be a full moon again, and in a few days, it will be a crescent moon again. This cycle, I don't know when it will end. Looking at it now, it is almost Mid-Autumn Festival again. Thinking about how the previous Mid-Autumn Festivals passed, it is still very clear. One Mid-Autumn Festival was spent with my mother in the courtyard worshiping the moon. I didn't seem to know what mysterious things were in the moon. My mother said that there were pine trees and gods in the moon. I raised my head and stared for a while. A very bright ball was speeding across the clear sky like water. Sure enough, it seemed like a pine tree filled most of the ball. I felt inexplicably happy. Another Mid-Autumn Festival made an even deeper impression. It was the first day I stepped onto the thorny path of life. I carried a small suitcase alone and stepped onto the deck of a ship. It was raining in the sky, and the deck was slippery. As soon as I got on the ship, I lowered my head and went into the cabin. I forgot that today was Mid-Autumn Festival. I didn't expect to wake up in the middle of the night. The sailors were playing mahjong, and the cracking sounds were so annoying. So I went back to the deck to take a look. The rain had stopped, and the moon was in the middle of the sea. The sea water was like silver snakes dancing, shaking the moon in the sky as if it were swaying. Painters cannot paint this scene, and I cannot write this scene. This is a magnificent view of the universe. I forgot where I was, I forgot why I left home this time, and I didn't even know that today was Mid-Autumn Festival. If I had remembered that today was Mid-Autumn Festival, you can imagine, "Every holiday makes me miss my relatives even more." People were eating mooncakes at home, while I was a wandering traveler, and I wouldn't know where to shed tears. Fortunately, I didn't remember that today was Mid-Autumn Festival at the time. Another Mid-Autumn Festival was in Qingdao, another Mid-Autumn Festival was in Shenyang. Each year is very clear. Now, although the moonlight is still the same as before, things have changed. It is no longer possible to spend the Mid-Autumn Festival like before.

The moon gradually rose. I had already turned into a small alley. Suddenly, walking from a busy and lively street to a dark alley, I felt unusually desolate and lonely. Turning back, I heard the sharp sound of car horns on the street, which felt like a lifetime ago, as if I had just woken up from a dream, and my nerves were a bit hazy. For some reason, the poem by Lu You that I read the day before yesterday also flooded into my mind: "The lights of the nearby workshops are as bright as books, the east wind blows the city sounds for ten miles, the distant workshops are silent and the doors are closed, only the smoke and moon are walked by no one... Returning to the empty study, I lie down feeling cold, the sick bones in front of the lamp cast a steep shadow..."

After arriving home, my wife asked me why I looked so depressed. I said it was nothing, probably just feeling a bit unwell. My wife didn't say anything. I didn't eat dinner and fell asleep in bed.

A Group of Hungry People 188

— Tianji

Seesaw (8) 189

— Bai Chen

The little monk couldn't drag the bed board. The little tots were busy, sweated all over, only then moved it out from the outside. He put the stool in the very middle, and the two of them, exerting their strength, moved the bed board onto the stool. One end near the bed, the other near the side of the stove. The little monk pressed down on this end, the other end popped up. He pressed down on the other end, this one popped up. The two of them were having so much fun. The little monk, pointing at the end near the bed: "Come on!"

The little tot laughed and jumped. The little monk became even more pleased. He held down that end of the board: "Climb on slowly!" Waiting for his little sister to sit down properly, then he himself climbed on.

"Why doesn't it seesaw?" the little monk pondered for a while.

The little tot, unable to wait, shouted, shaking her body, "Move, move!"

Hey, now they were able to move it. As the little sister got on, he got off, making them both scared and having fun. The two of them opened their mouths wide, clutching the bed board tightly, gently moving, and they gently went up and down.

"Ha! So much fun!" the little tot wanted to clap her hands, but afraid she would fall down, she grabbed the bed board tightly, just smiling.

"High! High!" The little monk remembered that other people seesawed much higher.

The little tot didn't know how to go higher. After thinking for a long while, the little monk told her, "Use strength!"

Sure enough, using strength made it seesaw higher. The little monk was extremely happy. He exerted even more strength. The little tot was a little scared, "Brother, slower!"

Who knew that the board was a little disobedient, it couldn't slow down. The little tot shouted in a panic; upon hearing her shout, the little monk also panicked. The bed board shot towards the little monk's end, and the little tot fell down, colliding into the little monk, and by sheer chance, her head hit the edge of the iron pot of the stove behind them. Fresh blood immediately flowed. "Wah!" the little tot cried.

The little monk, who had fallen on the ground, with the bed board pressing on his leg, crawled out from under his little sister, but could no longer stand up. Seeing the blood on his little sister's head, flowing like a small river, he was scared out of his mind. He pressed down on the wound, but his leg was unable to move. The blood still flowed like that.

The little tot shouted, "Mom..." her voice getting lower and lower as she shouted.

The little monk also shouted, "Mom!..." his voice getting more and more tragic as he shouted.

The sound was extremely terrible, but Mom still hadn't come back. (The End)

On Tangerines (Part 2) 190

— Chen Zizhan

Speaking of Florida tangerines, I have a connection with them.

It must be said that on July 6, 1930, my wife, Jingyi, suddenly took a turn for the worse due to intestinal disease and was rushed to the Red Cross General Hospital to be operated on by Dr. Ji Geng. She barely survived, and fortunately, after being hospitalized for a month, she managed to keep her life. At that time, my youngest boy, Shen'er, had just been born for eight months and had not yet been weaned. With his mother in the hospital, what could be done with this nursing child? When a wet nurse was hired, he looked at her, but wouldn't eat. When milk powder was mixed and put in a bottle, he sucked once, then refused to suck anymore. He was happy to drink a small bowl of rice broth with sugar. After drinking it for a few days, he didn't drink it anymore. He especially liked to drink rice broth mixed with a little chicken or fish soup, which had a salty taste. Only at night, when there was nothing to give him to eat, would he cry almost the whole night. One night, I bought a Florida tangerine, peeled it and put the segments into his mouth one by one. He was extremely happy, sucking on the tangerine segments as if they were nipples. He could eat two or three segments at a time. When he cried, I would give him tangerines to eat, and that night could be considered a comfortable one for him. From then on, I gave him tangerines to eat every night as milk. He ate eight or nine dollars worth of Florida tangerines a month, which was almost the same as the money spent on hiring a wet nurse. As a result, he became a small consumer of American tangerines, and I also developed a liking for eating this kind of tangerine.

Many years ago, I was extremely thin and would cough whenever I caught a cold. There was a suspicion of lung disease. As the saying goes, "One tangerine holds phlegm," so even if I had good tangerines, I didn't dare to eat too many. In fact, the saying has no basis. According to old medical books, dried tangerine peel and the white fibers of the tangerine are both things that help digestion and dissolve phlegm. It is said that there was a tangerine tree in the Yamen of Huazhou in Guangdong. Eating the tangerine peel boiled in soup could immediately dissolve phlegm and stop coughing. To this day, Huazhou tangerine peel is still recognized as a special medicine for dissolving phlegm and relieving coughs in Chinese medicine. There was another reason why I didn't dare to eat tangerines. I had suffered from stomach problems for more than ten years. Western doctors said it was hyperacidity, and I didn't dare to eat too many acidic things. Some Western doctors said, "Those who eat too many tangerines often suffer from acidic diseases, causing the body's tissues to have an acidic reaction. To cure this disease, one must abstain from eating tangerine juice." My wife, Jingyi, had suffered from stomach problems and had to avoid eating acidic things. She absolutely dared not taste tangerines. Later, a Western doctor advised us to try eating tangerines, saying that if eating tangerines did not worsen our gastrointestinal problems, then it would be best to eat more tangerines. It is said that "tangerine acid is an organic acid. Once it enters the intestines, it is decomposed and loses its acidity, instead having an alkaline reaction. Tangerine juice contains many minerals, such as calcium, phosphorus, iron, potassium, sodium, chlorine, and sulfur, especially potassium, which can enhance alkalinity. Therefore, eating too many tangerines will not cause acidity. Furthermore, tangerines contain a lot of vitamin C, and the sugars in tangerines are easy to digest. The vitamin content of tangerines also has the effect of stimulating bowel movements, which is really valuable. Therefore, it is good to eat more tangerines." After I ate tangerines, my stomach problems didn't change, so I advised my wife to eat them too. At first, my wife hesitated and didn't dare to try it easily. Only once, when she wanted to eat them, she ate half a Florida tangerine and felt very comfortable in her stomach. Afterwards, if she didn't eat tangerines after a meal, she felt uncomfortable. Therefore, tangerines became a daily fruit for our family, accounting for a large proportion of our daily consumption. However, in order to treat our illnesses, we couldn't worry about so much.

According to a folklore in Hunan, there is a well in the Chenzhou area, surrounded by tangerine trees, so it is called Tangerine Well. A Taoist named Su and his old mother lived next to the well. One day, the Taoist Su said to his old mother, "Mother, I am going to become an immortal. I think there will definitely be a plague next year. Only the well water here, boiled with one tangerine leaf, can cure the disease." After the Taoist Su said this, he ascended to heaven. The following year, a plague did break out, and nine out of ten people died. Only those who had eaten the well water and tangerine leaf soup as instructed by Su's old mother recovered from their illnesses. To this day, many pharmacies in Hunan still hang signboards with the inscriptions "Tangerine Well Flowing Spring" or "Tangerine Well Sprouting Spring." When people in Hunan talk about tangerines, they still don't forget this story.

Now it is autumn again. From the end of autumn to the beginning of winter, red tangerines enter the market. But I don't know if the tangerine orchard at my old residence under Mount Yuelu is still bearing abundant fruit, both green and yellow, and ripe? Alas, that was more than ten years ago!

Page 17

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Is Bizarre Clothing Detrimental to Public Morality? 191

— Meng Ruo

The customs of the north and south of China seem to be contagious to each other. Not long after Guangzhou banned co-ed swimming, Beijing followed suit. As soon as Beijing banned co-ed schools, there was a rumor that Guangzhou would do the same. Recently, the two places have unexpectedly begun to ban bizarre clothing.

Beijing: On the evening of July 30th, at the Harbin Theater, about ten policemen carrying box cannons and small pistols swarmed in and ordered all modern women wearing clothes as thin as cicada wings and bare legs without socks to leave the theater, not allowed to watch the show, and to return after changing clothes. At the same time, there were also policemen guarding outside the door, and all women with bizarre clothing were stopped, without exception. In general, modern women could only hang their heads and return home, and the amusing scene came to an end.

Guangzhou: A few days ago, the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau issued a clothing standard, advising women to abide by it, and ordering Western clothing stores not to make new-style clothes in the future. They also sent female propaganda teams to give speeches in public places. But after more than ten days of implementation, there were still women wearing bizarre clothing and strutting through the streets everywhere. The Public Security Bureau believes that compulsory enforcement is necessary to be effective, so they decided to strictly ban it from September 1st. Those who resist will be taken to the bureau for investigation.

Recently, because there are so many people in our country who are open-minded about customs, a group of women has been very unlucky. In our eyes, so-called bizarre clothing is just a relatively new style, and there is no need to make a fuss about it. If we want to promote thrift and make a correction, there are some reasons to be said. But some people always point to this as detrimental to public morality, and unless it is strictly prohibited, there will be no way to restore the world's morals and people's hearts. This kind of view is too pedantic. We really don't believe that a new-style clothing will cause damage to morals and physical health. Most Western women are bare-legged and bare-chested, but we have never seen them damage public morality because of this. Is it true that Chinese people are all lustful, and they will have evil thoughts as soon as they see a certain part of a woman's body? This is truly a disgrace to the Chinese people. Taking a step back, even if bizarre clothing is considered seductive, it can only be dealt with through persuasion. It seems unnecessary to threaten with guns, and compulsory enforcement is not a proper method.

We still remember that in March last year, a so-called modern vandalism incident occurred in Hangzhou. A group of hooligans used nitric acid to damage women's clothes everywhere. This barbaric act was quickly banned by the authorities. However, the President of the Executive Yuan, Wang Jingwei, specifically issued a statement to explain the meaning of modern, saying that modern is modern. It can be seen that modern is not a sin, so why should we hate it so much? In fact, there are many things in society that harm public morality, and it is impossible to ban them all. Bizarre clothing, in the final analysis, has little to do with public morality. If the authorities must use all their strength to deal with it, it is really a waste of effort.

Yu Shanfu 192

— Shi Weizhi

Two Sculptures of People

Yu Shanfu, he is my senior apprentice, — I rely on my father's remaining influence — to have such a senior apprentice.

His leg is somewhat broken, so his name is not as famous as his congenital illness. People generally call him "Crippled Leg," at most, some people know his name is Shanfu, so they call him "Crippled Leg Shanfu." As for his surname, only a very few people know.

He is a very good person, sincere and enthusiastic. Whenever something happens, he is willing to put his work aside to help others. He often gets fired from his job for being nosy, but after losing his job, he doesn't blame anyone. He must finish that matter before trying to find another job.

Because of this, he is often criticized behind his back by other senior apprentices who think they are smart, "The emperor is not worried, but the eunuch is anxious," rushing around like a headless fly, what good is it?

But when those senior apprentices who think they are smart have something happen, they will look for Shanfu.

Although Senior Apprentice Shanfu had heard of this shortcoming before, as long as someone finds him and asks him for help, he will still run around enthusiastically.

He said, if fellow apprentices don't help each other, who else can you ask to help? Although he knows that helping will not benefit him at all, and sometimes it will even "bring someone else's coffin to your own home" (note), he still runs around regardless.

Sometimes, meddling in other people's affairs gets himself into trouble. In the end, the person involved will secretly say behind his back, "It's all because of 'Crippled Leg,' the matter could have been resolved long ago, but he got in the way, and now there is still no conclusion."

Naturally, he is very unhappy to hear this. After the matter is resolved, he swears to himself: in the future

Page 18

may my sons and grandsons be damned if I meddle in other people's business again, I'm just making enemies for myself, doing all the work and then getting kicked to the curb, can't I just live a peaceful life?

But after some time, when someone else comes to find him, he forgets the oath he made.

His work skills are not very high, and he also likes to meddle in other people's business. Often, after working in a shop for only a few days, he gets asked to "help," so he puts aside the unfinished work for ten days or half a month. Therefore, when colleagues in Shanghai hear someone mention Crippled Leg Shanfu, they all shake their heads. Some people will even say to the person who came, Crippled Leg, his skills are not very good, and he also likes to meddle in other people's business, our shop is small, we really don't have room for him.

In this way, he usually works in our shop for half a year each year.

Working in our shop is also something he can't help. Because the fellow apprentices look down on him, they often make fun of him with cold words, and he is also somewhat afraid of my father.

Because he can't stand being restrained, and he is used to being a wild horse, so after some time, his ambition can't be suppressed, so he says:

"Master, I want to go to the outer docks to look for work, I heard that the market in ×× is very good recently."

Every time, my father always smiles and doesn't say yes or no: "You always have to be steady, you're over thirty years old, and you still like to meddle in other people's business like a seventeen or eighteen year old, the outer docks are unfamiliar, you have to be even more steady."

After my father leaves, he says to himself as if talking to himself: "Master is still saying the same old things, treating me like I'm three years old," and then, he happily says to me, "Younger brother, I'll write to you when I get to ××."

That night, his whereabouts are unknown. The next afternoon, he takes the tool cart away.

In this way, it has become a routine. When the neighbors see him taking the tool cart, they jokingly say: "Crippled Leg, are you going to open up a new dock again?"

Three days after my mother died, he somehow got the news, bought some paper ingots and incense candles, rushed over, kowtowed in front of my mother's coffin, and the first thing he asked was:

"Where is the mistress's coffin placed?"

After being told where the coffin was, I wrote a note and put it in my pocket, saying that although he was one step late and didn't see the mistress's last moments, he still had to see the coffin to feel at ease.

Since that meeting, we haven't met for three whole years. A few days ago, I ran into him on the road. He has changed his profession and is making a living by selling crickets. Before parting, he said: "Younger brother, do you still raise crickets recently? I have a very good one here, you can take it back to play with, it's just that the children here don't know what it's worth."

When I replied that I hadn't raised crickets for many years, he smiled and said, "I forgot, you are an adult now."

(Note: "Bringing someone else's coffin to your own home" means getting involved in other people's affairs.)

Sketches of Beiping 193

— Meng Hua

(1) Escorting the Prisoner

It was a gloomy day after the snow.

Outside Qianmen, many idlers were crowding around, their faces excited. Their breathing made them sound like trains arriving at a station, with hot air puffing from their noses.

"Going to Tianqiao to see the execution!"

The children shouted loudly. The people standing on both sides of the road craning their necks and looking anxiously at the dark crowd behind them.

"Here it comes! Here!" All kinds of uneven voices flowed out of the mouths of the audience unconsciously. Like a famous actor coming on stage, thousands of arrows of eyes shot at the car behind.

The police car escorting the way slowly drove past. The police riding on horses swung their wooden sticks to drive away pedestrians in the street. "Get out of the way! Hey, get out of the way!" The people riding on horses shouted sternly. This was their proudest moment.

Following behind were three spacious trucks. A prisoner was standing on the truck. At this moment, cheers rose from all directions.

The prisoner standing on the truck easily unbuttoned his coat, the corners of his coat fluttering in the north wind. He was a strong man with a dark complexion, his piercing eyes scanning the crowd standing on the sidewalk.

"Sing a song!" Someone asked the prisoner.

A smile floated on the man's face. Then he straightened his voice and sang a martial artist's tune:

"I, a hero... in the past..." The voice sounded particularly tragic in the north wind.

"Good! Good!" The road was like a stage, and the cheers were like a rainstorm.

At the entrance of a restaurant, the car stopped:

"Hey, shopkeeper, I want a catty of baijiu!"

"What a true hero!" The old bannerman carrying a birdcage exclaimed in admiration.

"That's right! A few days ago, two opium addicts were executed, looking dejected, it wasn't exciting to watch," said a young shop assistant standing next to him.

After the sound of the crowd followed the man and faded away, the remaining snow on the road had all melted into water, leaving behind a muddy street.

(2) Garbage Dump

Have you seen a garbage dump? This is a rare decoration of Beiping's city appearance.

At the end of a slightly secluded alley, and even in front of several university gates, there are such garbage dumps. Next to it, there is often a pool of verdigris-colored stagnant water, with mosquitoes leisurely floating in it.

Every day from early morning until dusk, some sanitation workers wearing red uniforms slowly push their dirt carts and dump the garbage here. Moldy vegetables, rotten intestines and stomachs, dead cats, dead chickens, and dead rats with fleas jumping and maggots wriggling pile up into a small mountain. The June sun steams it, the northwest wind carries it, and the neighbors all get this benefit.

However, many people also rely on this garbage dump to survive.

Similarly, from dawn until dusk, children, old ladies, and young girls also wriggle on this garbage dump like maggots. Most of them carry a broken basket in their hands, picking up coal balls, paper scraps, rags, canned food, broken glass bottles, etc. They use their hands, small bamboo whips, and concentrate on turning, picking, and snatching. Their hair has lost its black and shiny color, and grease has stuck it together. The children's heads and bodies are covered with sores, and they smear their ragged clothes with their stool and snot. Crows and dogs are also their common friends.

These are the ones who live on the things that people throw away! Especially the children, they suffer from the cold, they go hungry, they have no health.

Unnamed Grass 194

— Qin Jian

I don't know when, and I don't know why, but I finally vaguely felt the existence of autumn.

During the day, I give my whole body and soul to the control of life, but at night, the disturbances of the day have completely disappeared. People exhale uneven breaths from their deep sleep, and leak out wisps of sobs and cries from their nightmares, as if they are extremely unwilling to remember the various worries of the world forever, or, at the very least, they are trying to secretly express the many grievances of life in their dreams—between these, there are many resentments and shames hidden: they are suppressed by the weight of life, day and night.

Even so: but the world is still quiet. How calm and quiet the night is: when people wake up in this empty night, a terrible loneliness and emptiness, like the heavy rain and lightning of summer nights, attack again and again: I feel every breath of day and night, and I also seem to feel every pulse of the night, all of which have such heavy and gloomy postures? I am afraid and worried, because I clearly understand and truly feel: the night is sinking inch by inch: it is getting deeper every moment. That kind of depth: is pitch black and has no end, thinking about it will make you feel suffocated!

Worriedly looking out the window at the road and the sky: the road is so dim that it is impossible to tell the direction; and the sky is still a desolate pitch black, from which the stars flicker and die out one by one. Is it impossible to find any news of dawn?

Feeling an unusual suffocation, feeling the vastness of the night, the news of dawn cannot be predicted, and the end of the night is difficult to anticipate, groping to let the soul fall into the bottomless pit, sinking down moment by moment, that is not a comfortable thing.

(Autumn, and autumn has already grown up - midnight in autumn is uncomfortable: a little lonely light, a string of intermittent chirps of insects and wind. A train passes from afar with faces full of wind and dust, weakly venting one or two sounds - as soon as I hear this, I can imagine the way it crawls through the wilderness - it has carried so many people, and how hard it has traveled so many journeys, no one knows to ask about it: and now, it is calling out tiredly and angrily.)

Then, the green romances of one's own past life - those hardships, insults, and taunts - fall lightly on the barren land of memory like a light dream before dawn, from blurry to clear, like a "dissolve" in a movie.

So I think: cherish yourself, pursue yourself, review yourself in the past days.

But, in the end, I doubted again: what am I? What is the past? What should the past self be?

The more I try to figure it out, the more confused I become, the thoughts in my mind are stirred into a mess by something: I even began to doubt the world, doubt humanity, and even doubt the whole of life!

Haven't some people said that doubt and speculation are automatic, immune "life diseases" that everyone from young to old must suffer from? If this is true, then how long will this dark and gloomy mood last, and when will my heart, like the sky on an autumn night, faintly reveal the dawn?

I am afraid, I am flustered, and finally, I hope - may this dissolution and collapse of the youth's belief in the world be just a nightmare before the long night is over, and when dawn breaks, it will disappear invisibly.

Even if, at present, it is still an unnamed black night - with endless desolation and length.
