Shen Bao Local Supplement - Automobile Weekly

Campbell's Amazing Car Record, 300 Miles Per Hour 206

— Yu

Average of 11.955 Seconds Per Mile. "Blue Bird" Breaks Four Previous Records.

Sir Malcolm Campbell, known as the "Speed King of England," held another car speed race near the Bonneville Salt Flats in Utah, USA, on September 3rd. As a result, he not only broke his previous highest record, but also reached his lifelong wish of 300 miles per hour. This is not only a personal success for Sir Campbell, but also a memorable event in the history of automobile speed. The official figure for this speed record is 301.1292 miles per hour. The record for 1934 was 276.816 miles per hour.

"Blue Bird" is the name of the car driven by Sir Campbell. The previous four records were also established by "Blue Bird." However, from 1931 to 1935, this car underwent a degree of improvement and innovation each time it set a new record. The engine also gradually increased in size. Now, the words "Blue Bird" and Campbell's record will be immortalized together.

When Sir Campbell drove on the Bonneville Salt Flats on the morning of September 3rd, members of the American Automobile Association were on site to record the speed and time. The initial speed announced by the timer was 299.874 miles per hour, which was still a little short of Campbell's hoped-for record. However, the difference was very small. Later, the timekeeper of the American Automobile Association discovered that there was a slight error in the timing. In fact, Campbell had exceeded the 300-mile record. Therefore, the association announced on the same day that the previous record of 299.874 was in error and corrected it to 301.1292 miles per hour. However, before the official disclosure of the mileage, some American newspapers reported it as 300.377 miles per hour. Soon all were corrected.

During the race, there was a dangerous incident. If it were not for Campbell's iron will and skill in driving, a major accident would have been inevitable. Campbell was able to get through such dangers safely and could be congratulated. As he was about to reach the finish line, the car had entered the limit mileage and was moving southwest. Suddenly, the front tire of that huge car burst. At this time, the speed of the "Blue Bird" was 280 miles per hour. We can imagine with our eyes closed how dangerous it was. If the wheels were slightly skewed or went off the track, Campbell would have been smashed to pieces. Fortunately, he did not panic and was very calm, keeping his eyes on the steering wheel and moving forward along the track. He finally overcame the difficult obstacle.

Campbell set the 300-mile record when he ran into the limit mileage. At that time, the car was heading northeast and the time was 11.83 seconds. The calculated speed of the car was 304.311 miles per hour. This figure broke the odd number of the American aircraft speed record. That record was 304.98 miles per hour, which was created by the late Mr. Whitell on September 4, 1933, in Granville, Illinois. Sir Campbell then moved southwest at a speed of 12.08 seconds per mile. The calculated speed was 298.013. These two records gave him an average time of 11.955 seconds in the limit mileage, obtaining a record of 301.1292 miles per hour.

The environment was very good on the day of the drive. The ground and visibility were good, but there was a slight breeze, which was a minor flaw. The wind reduced the forward speed of the "Blue Bird" by about 9 miles per hour. Since the disclosure of Campbell's 300-mile record, congratulatory telegrams have been sent from all over the world. Notable among them are the British Minister of Transport, Leslie Hore-Belisha, the British oil magnate, and sports celebrity Lord Wakefield. Campbell's creation of this 300-mile record is regarded as a great honor and a rare achievement in automobile driving and sports.

The 1934 record (276.816 miles per hour) was set on the Daytona Beach. At that time, Campbell stated that what he wished to achieve was 300 miles per hour, and that the day he reached this record would be the day he would no longer drive. Because this kind of driving is really a very dangerous thing. Campbell can be said to have achieved his wish this time. After the race ended on that day, Campbell said that he had to go through New York to board a ship to return to England on September 9th. After returning to England this time, Campbell will probably no longer drive on adventures. Campbell's courage is truly admirable.

Sir Campbell's five-ton "Blue Bird I" this time has a very magnificent appearance. The head is flat and wind-breaking, and the whole body is in the shape of a low rectangle. The front two wheels are single wheels, and the rear wheels are double wheels. The engine power is more stable than the last time in Daytona. In the one-mile journey, this "Blue Bird" takes less than 12 seconds to walk. The structure of this car is enough to stand out from all the vehicles in the world.

In the most recent 32 years, the speed of land vehicles has increased from the initial 68 miles per hour to Campbell's current 300 miles per hour. The difference has increased by almost five times. The records created by Campbell in the last five years are as follows. The average speed in 1931 was 206 miles per hour. In 1932 it was 245.733 miles per hour. In 1933 it was 253.968 miles per hour. In 1934 it was 253.6 miles per hour. In 1935 it was 299.874 miles per hour.

Review of Automobile Mechanisms and Noise Reduction Movements 207

— Ying Dai

In the last year or two, the transportation authorities of various Western countries have paid great attention to the issue of noise reduction. In noisy cities, nine out of ten times the noise is extraordinary, which is annoying. Therefore, the authorities of various countries advocate noise reduction. In the noise reduction movement, one point that is worth mentioning here is that a car can also emit annoying noises at any time when driving on the street. In order to implement the noise reduction movement, what kind of method should we take to reduce the sound of cars driving? Mr. Beileshi, the Director of Transportation in London, appointed a number of experts as soon as he took office to study the causes of various sounds emitted by vehicles driving on the streets and to find ways to eliminate or reduce them. This committee was chaired by Henry Fowler. After several months of research, it was determined that using scientific methods to manufacture cars can reduce a portion of the noise from driving. If car factories can manufacture cars according to the principles they have set, then such cars can travel on the streets in any season of the year without annoying noises. If the Director of Transportation follows the principles they have set, then when registering new cars, many more regulations will be added to restrict the noise of cars. First, the internal combustion engine must be equipped with an effective muffler, and drivers must not allow it to make bursting sounds. When we recall, in 1933, more than 8,000 drivers in London were detained and fined for making improper noises with their cars. At that time, these regulations had already been included. However, the authorities did not pay attention to how effective the so-called effective muffler was when registering cars. It was nothing more than theory. From now on, regarding this point, it has been decided to make it a reality from theory. It is necessary to stipulate the effect of the muffler. At the same time, on the other hand, we are looking forward to the cooperation of general car factories so that the cars they manufacture can all reach a standard of quietness above a certain level.

The London authorities once designated a quiet area for testing. The results have proved that when the noise is reduced, the number of car accident cases can also be reduced. However, in addition to the mechanical aspects of the car and the driver, which can reduce noise, the noise of trams cannot be eliminated and is very annoying. Therefore, the London transportation authorities have now decided to use another type of silent electric car to replace the old trams. The results of the trial of this electric car have been quite effective. Therefore, the authorities have decided that in the coming year, 40 miles of tram lines in London can be replaced by silent electric cars. Whether this plan can be realized depends not only on whether the drivers and car manufacturing engineers meet the standards set by scientific principles, but also on whether people's actions and behaviors have moral creeds. This is a problem that electricity meters and car factories cannot control. Drivers, fast learning, noise, can always be careful and cautious, and can pay attention to public morality, then the so-called noise reduction problem, regarding the car part, will not be difficult to solve.

The fact has long been proven. The more disturbing the car's mechanical components and noise, the easier it is to cause accidents. A reckless or technically mediocre driver driving a car with bursting sounds is definitely very loud, and the number of accidents is also more than other drivers. Therefore, in the United Kingdom, the transportation authorities have decided to require cities to maintain a considerable quiet standard for car and horse traffic. Today's cars have undoubtedly reduced a lot of noise compared to the iron-wheeled carriages of the past. But we should still go a step further and reduce the noise of cars to a minimum in order to reduce the car accident record. It is very difficult to install a muffler on a locomotive due to its small size, but it is easy in a car. At present, reducing the noise from the exhaust of various parts of the car is an urgent and important issue. Because this kind of noise is the most ear-splitting. In recent years, car factories have been working hard to reduce the bursting sound of the exhaust to a minimum. They already know that a good car must have a good and quiet exhaust. In this era, people are indeed tired of the noise of nineteen out of ten. And to make the noise reduction movement a reality, cooperation between the transportation authorities and car factories is an undeniable thing.

Germany's Automobile Industry Under Hitler's Support 208

— Qin

A recent report from the Berlin Automobile Association stated that Germany's automobile industry is now second in Europe in terms of quantity, and first in Europe in terms of scientific inspection of its products. It will soon compete with the United States across the Atlantic, etc. Germany's automobile industry has indeed made rapid progress in recent years, and it is not just general public relations rhetoric.

It is generally recognized that the reason why the German automobile industry has been able to make such progress is due to the support of the German leader Hitler for the automobile industry. When the Berlin Auto Show opened last month, German scientists gathered together. Mr. Hitler took the stage and gave a speech on the German government's dedicated development of the automobile industry and told a story, which shows the general importance Germany attaches to the automobile industry. Hitler's story is very meaningful and moving. The full text is as follows.

"Decades ago, there was a British resident in India who was very good at economic planning for daily necessities. This person was also good at managing cars. At that time, he had two exquisite cars. When driving, he often felt that the construction of Indian roads was poor, and the damage to the cars was very significant. Therefore, he petitioned the Indian government to improve the construction of roads. However, the Indian rulers at that time were slow to deal with matters and believed that if the roads were poor, it was not necessary to drive cars. They turned a blind eye. This person continued to apply to rebuild the roads, but never received a reply. This person was extremely angry and added various criticisms, but the Indian government still ignored him. Later, this person ran out of ideas and thought of a plan. He sent a beautiful car to the Indian King. The Indian King was very happy and drove this beautiful car on the streets every day. Unexpectedly, the car was destroyed soon. He asked the Englishman why the car was so beautiful but so easily damaged. The Englishman told him that it was because the roads were poor. The Indian King immediately ordered the local officials to improve the roads and hired 10,000 road workers to manage the matter. In a few days, all the roads in India were improved and completed, and this Englishman's plan was successful. Later, cars could be driven safely. However, the Indian government's neglect of the automobile industry soon led to the disaster of national subjugation. Even if it was not destroyed by this, it was also a considerable cause."

Hitler told this story to ridicule the Indian government's lack of construction, which led to the tragedy of national subjugation, and to encourage Germans to build. Hitler usually believes that life is short and time is precious. The time we spend on the road when we are engaged in our duties is very regrettable. Therefore, he advocates widely popularizing transportation equipment. In the 20th century, the only important means of transportation on land other than trains is cars. Therefore, Hitler is sparing no effort to promote the automobile industry. The reason why Germany's automobile industry has reached such a point today is also due to Hitler's support from above and the efforts of the German people from below.

Hitler's plan to support the automobile industry can be divided into three items. One is to make cars economically popular so that everyone in Germany has the possibility of riding in a car. One is to design roads meticulously to maintain safety and extend the life of the car. One is to make the car's parts strong, be practical and realistic, and not be flashy. The initial work is to prevent the import of cars into Germany. All Germans use German cars, and then promote them to other countries to make people know the advantages of German cars and compete with the automobile industries of other countries.

Recently, Hitler has united people in the automobile industry to jointly establish a car factory and hire unemployed workers to manufacture cars. Among the goals he has set, there is a flexible small car named Bangmei Pagmy, which means short and powerful. This car has been widely seen in all parts of Germany, and has also been seen in European countries. It is low in price and good in quality, but the appearance is not rich. However, the general public is happy to buy and use it. On the market in Berlin today, three or four out of every ten cars are this car. The car body shape of this car is very small, and the fuel consumption is very economical. It is suitable for long or short journeys. The high speed can reach 50 miles per hour. Nowadays, European car buyers who want to buy a small car will definitely consider Bangmei cars as their first goal. It can be seen that this car will soon gradually invade the markets of Asia and the Americas from Europe.

Hitler's road plan has been arranged. Every city in Germany can be reached directly by car roads, and there are gas stations all over the road, so there is no need to worry about running out of gas halfway. This project has attracted the attention of rulers of various countries, and the United Kingdom has also started to follow in Hitler's footsteps. Then, Hitler's desire to make Germany's automobile industry dominate the world is within the realm of possibility.

The left picture shows the Ford V8 bus sold by the Hong Kong Ford Manager's Office to the Bank of China in Guiyang 209

Ford is Pleased to Publish Production Data 210

Dearborn, Michigan, July 12th. Today, Henry Ford provided newspaper representatives with the production figures for the first six months of this year and said with a smile, "Recently, my biggest job is to distribute wealth so that the people can use it."

Last November, Ford declared that he would produce "one million or more" cars in 1935. Only half of the year has passed, and the total number of cars produced by Ford Motor Company in the United States and Canada by June 30 has reached 810,700. The number of cars manufactured abroad during the same period was 37,804, for a total of 848,504 units produced worldwide. Someone asked Ford, "When do you hope to exceed the one million unit mark?"

This car manufacturer, who was wearing a tan and noble costume at the time, smiled again and said, "Now, that's another question. I am just a manufacturer, not a prophet. My staff has work to do. This is what our entire organization is grateful for. There are still many things that make us hopeful for the next six months, but we cannot be completely sure. We can only do our best within the scope of what is possible."

Although Ford himself remained silent and made no predictions, Mr. Gao Lin's speech to a Ford dealership in Lichimeng on Tuesday stated that the new slogan "one million or more in 1935" has been adopted. This meeting was one of a series of meetings being convened across the United States. Accompanying Mr. Gao Lin were Heckins, the Deputy Manager of the Sales Department, Hanchi, the Manager of the Lincoln Sales Department, Cooper of Ford Motor Company Limited in the United Kingdom, and Bachowitz, the Business Development Manager of Global Credit Company, a joint education company that sells Ford products.
